## 2026-06-02 — Em reference-images: give the critic the Bible (code shipped; live re-baseline deferred)

**What changed (branch `feature/em-reference-images`, isolated worktree off `main` @ `458b248`):** addressed the locked #1 critic-spine fix — Em was **reference-blind** (judged frames against text only; never read `ctx.criteria`). Em now reads **references + criteria**. Four test-pinned code seams + the case-7 flip, all TDD'd and credential-free: (1) `cli_runners.RateCapExhausted` — `agy` writes its 429 to its *log* and returns exit-0 empty stdout, so the stderr-only scan reported `ok=True` and silently degraded every frame to `borderline` during quota exhaustion; the wrapper now **raises** on empty-stdout-exit-0 *or* an explicit quota signal, kept distinct from a non-empty-malformed response (defensive-borderline) (`41f2eca`). (2) `pipeline/agents/reference_selection.py::select_references` — a fixed, Bible-driven, capped bundle (anchor + ≤`cap` deduped turnarounds, front/3-quarter/profile), resolved *from* the Bible (folder via `character.yaml`, turnarounds globbed + view-ranked), generalizes to any character; eval == prod; `checkpoint`/`beat` accepted-but-ignored (approach-A seam) (`864484d`). (3) `vision_critic.run` attaches `[subject, *references]` to **both** the Gemini default and Opus escalation paths (incl. phase-6 contact sheets) + an ordering block (subject = image 1); `character_id` absent → graceful no-references (`288dc91`). (4) `vision_critic._criteria_block` surfaces `query_by_character ∩ query_by_phase` from the merged `CriteriaBundle` as a "cite these by ID" block; graceful on `None`/empty (`7ed1ae3`). (5) **case-7 flipped xfail → green** (`evals/character_designer/`) — validity (Em's real input keys), `IR.sean.*` ID alignment (canonical; folder key `sean-anchor` ≠ `character_id` `sean`), and a prompt-reading mock that cites whatever IR rule the fix actually surfaced (`e47d375`). (6) eval re-wire for **structural parity** — `cases.yaml` gains `character_id`; harness + `score.py` call the *same* `select_references` + load the *same* bundle (`16695f4`).

**Two evidence-driven plan deviations (test never weakened):** the plan's turnaround matcher picked `body-3quarter-back` over `body-3quarter` (sort + substring) → fixed the *implementation* (exact-stem-match first); and case-7's `identity_critical` force-escalates to Opus, so the plan's Gemini-only mock left it red → mock both paths (one shared prompt). Both proven red-first.

**Tests:** `tests/` **264 passed** (242 + 6 rate-cap + 7 reference_selection + 5 references + 4 criteria); `evals/vision_critic/runner.py` green (motion cases xpass); `evals/character_designer/runner.py` **6 passed + 1 xpass** (case-7 now passed, one fewer xfail). `pipeline/tests/` green.

**The costed live re-baseline + three-way bake-off are DEFERRED** to a clean-terminal run — not for lack of correctness (the reference mechanism is **proven live at n=1**: `select_references` resolved the exact target bundle, attached it, and Em scored) but because the agent-harness execution environment fought the repeated-live-call pattern three distinct ways. Trilemma on this Python 3.14 + `agy`/Opus-CLI + agent-harness stack: single-process → asyncio teardown crash (exit 144, "Loop is closed") after case 1; subprocess isolation → the teardown signal propagates up the process group and kills the orchestrator mid-run; detaching the *workers* into a new session → orchestrator survives but **Claude Code auth breaks** for the Opus child (unparseable → `borderline` + empty cites → every case errors). Resolution shipped in `score.py`: subprocess-per-case isolation (verdict flushed to stdout *before* the worker's teardown crash, so it's captured regardless of exit code) + `--segment`/`--motion-smoke`/`--limit` scoping; **detach only the orchestrator at launch, never the workers** (`8a611d4`, `587c213`). A 2-case smoke confirmed orchestrator-detach survives multiple teardowns. Full narrative + the deferred-run recipe + disciplines: [`docs/anima-test-runs/2026-06-02-em-reference-images-field-report.md`](docs/anima-test-runs/2026-06-02-em-reference-images-field-report.md).

**Incident:** a `score.py --segment` run appeared from the *main checkout* (not any worktree launch this session) and vanished untraced — likely a parallel execution (idle session `22428` is cwd'd in main). No active collision, but it reinforces: costed runs need a single known owner (the same shared-tree hazard the critic-spine postmortem records).

**Why:** Em is the T2 critic Act 2's motion QA leans on; reference-blindness was its biggest measured flaw. Giving her the Bible (plates + criteria) is the structural fix. The code is done and proven; the *number* (the precision lift with false-pass held) is the one thing waiting on a clean run. Follow-ons unchanged: view-aware selection (A), pairwise reframe, DINOv2 backstop (promoted to next if any false pass appears).

## 2026-06-01 — Em critic-spine hardening: scored baseline, motion-sight, and the reference-blindness finding

**What changed (branch `feature/critic-spine-hardening`):** stood Em (T2 vision critic) up from "shipped, never scored" to a **scored, segmented, live baseline** against 29 labeled cases, plus an honest motion-sight path, plus an evidence-backed (if reference-blind + Gemini-quota-incomplete) three-way model read. Commits: contact-sheet builder + `phase_6_motion` honesty clause (`bda0fd5`); the `evals/vision_critic/` eval suite — `scoring.py` (precision/recall/false-pass on the defect class, segmented), `cases.yaml` (10 clean / 13 identity-style / 6 motion-proper-red, every input a real committed fixture), two-mode harness (CI-green mocked `runner.py` + deliberate live `score.py`), `failure-modes.md` (`0ab6e2d`); `invoke_sonnet_vision` via a model-parameterized `_invoke_vision` (`5f45ec5`); the three-way bake-off harness (`379fdfa`); Em now reviews raw clips via auto contact-sheet + `agy` `stdin=DEVNULL` (`c5b9dae`); `score.py` per-case resilience + a real `--stub` opt-out (`be82692`); concurrent bake-off scoring (`021a9ba`); locked labels + baseline + the finding (`af7950d`).

**The baseline (live: Gemini 3.1 Pro @ agy + Opus 4.7 escalation, 29 cases, 0 errored):** Performs segment (clean + identity/style, n=23) **precision 0.62, recall 1.00, false-pass 0.00**; motion-proper (n=6, expected-red) all flagged on style, never citing a motion criterion (the honesty clause working); overall precision 0.70 / recall 1.00 / false-pass 0.00. STOP GATE 2 live W1 verdict: `fail` @0.78 — caught Seedance background-regeneration across the strip, **explicitly deferred** line-stability to a human/deterministic pass.

**The load-bearing finding — Em is reference-blind.** She judges every frame against **text only**; `run()` attaches just the frame, no `anchor.png`/Bible plate/A-2, and `ctx.criteria` is never read. This explains the shape: recall 1.00 (gross breaks catch from text rules) but precision 0.62 (no anchor to license a confident `pass` → 8 false alarms on clean frames; Sean confirmed `clean_F13`/`clean_F31` are the correct Sean). Labels ratified UNCHANGED — the over-flagging is reference-blindness, not bad frames. **Giving Em reference images (+ loading the merged `CriteriaBundle`) is the locked #1 next fix** (`docs/anima-test-runs/2026-06-01-em-reference-blindness-FINDING.md`).

**Incident — concurrent agent on a shared tree.** A second Claude session was found executing this same plan in this same working copy (it committed Tasks 8 & 9 through the shared HEAD, edited shared files, left junk). It was shut down (after identifying our own PID to avoid self-termination); its commits were verified + kept, its junk cleaned. Lesson: run plan execution in an isolated git worktree. Also fixed in passing: `evals/character_designer/runner.py` monkeypatched the renamed `invoke_nb_pro` → `invoke_image_edit` (`ccc24a6`).

**Closed this session (bake-off + wrap, isolated worktree).** The live three-way bake-off ran: **Sonnet + Opus via the SDK are valid; the Gemini-via-agy column is INVALID** — Gemini's consumer-tier quota was exhausted mid-run (429 `RESOURCE_EXHAUSTED` in agy's log → empty stdout → Em's parser defaulted each call to `borderline`; 2.2s wall, TN=0, cites 0.00 are the tells). **Decision: T2 default unchanged** — the incumbent (Gemini) wasn't fairly on the field, and all three models are reference-blind, so the comparison can't license a swap; `manifest` untouched (`evals/bakeoffs/2026-05-31-t2-vision-critic-gemini-vs-sonnet-vs-opus/results.md`). On the *valid* columns, Sonnet mirrors the reference-blind baseline (false-pass 0.00, best cites 0.48) while Opus posts higher precision/agreement but **lets one real defect through** (`stylus-hand-f13-cc01` — false-pass 0.08, the costly error) by licensing passes it can't verify reference-blind. The bake-off surfaced a **second latent bug**: agy emits the 429 to its *log*, not stderr, so `cli_runners.run_antigravity_with_image` reports a quota-exhausted empty response as `ok=True` → a production live run during quota exhaustion would silently degrade every frame to `borderline` (fix folded into the reference-images workstream). Doc wrap done (this entry + the CLAUDE.md Em-row / `evals/vision_critic/` + `evals/bakeoffs/` directory map / two-mode eval commands). Full narrative: `docs/anima-test-runs/2026-06-01-em-critic-spine-hardening-postmortem.md` (its §Update carries the bake-off outcome). Tests: `tests/` **242 passed** (from 231 baseline). **The complete, valid three-way bake-off is deferred to the post-reference-fix session** (Gemini re-run after quota reset + the wrapper-bug fix + references attached).

**Why:** the critic Act 2's motion QA depends on had never been scored or shown a clip — this makes its quality empirical. The eval did its job: the ruler found the critic's biggest flaw (reference-blindness) with evidence, which is the real output of the session.

**What changed:** Ran the research mandated by the continuation prompt (entry below) and folded the verified method back into the critic-spine kickoff. Two deliverables:

1. **The findings doc** — [`docs/research/2026-05-31-ai-evals-best-practices-and-anima-eval-strategy.md`](docs/research/2026-05-31-ai-evals-best-practices-and-anima-eval-strategy.md). A cited, verified synthesis of 2026 AI-eval best practice translated into anima's context, studio-manual voice, 7-section spine (exec summary → first principles → LLM-as-judge calibration → metrics & tracking → tooling borrow-vs-build → the per-agent-type fleet eval-strategy matrix → sources). Research ran via the `deep-research` skill fanned across five angles with adversarial verification, primary/practitioner sources preferred (Hamel Husain, Shreya Shankar, Anthropic "Demystifying Agent Evals", Eugene Yan, Zheng et al., the arXiv LLM-as-judge canon, VBench/DreamBooth/FVMD for vision). **The load-bearing outcome: three of the five judge-bias numbers the brainstorm §2.5 cites were verified and CORRECTED** — sycophancy 58.19% *confirmed* (but it's sycophancy-under-rebuttal, not an unprompted base rate); self-preference *"+90%" dropped* (misattributed to arXiv 2410.02736, which is "Justice or Prejudice?/CALM" and doesn't contain it — the real mechanism paper is Panickssery/Bowman/Feng 2404.13076, no +90% magnitude); criteria-injection *"+3pp" uncited* (substitute Databricks Grading Notes' 67–85% misalignment cut); ensemble *"+9.8pp" corrected* to PoLL's Cohen's κ +0.136, 7× cheaper; position + length bias confirmed. The doc's §3.3 ledger is now the verified source the fleet is held to. Also decisive for the critic-spine work: the **"MLLMs pass shuffled frames"** finding (arXiv 2505.14321) → a frame-grid contact sheet lets Em see identity/style *across* a clip but **not motion-proper**; motion needs deterministic metrics (warping-error/VBench-set/FVMD) or an honest human seam.

2. **The kickoff fold-back** — surgically sharpened [`docs/2026-05-31-critic-spine-hardening-kickoff.md`](docs/2026-05-31-critic-spine-hardening-kickoff.md) (shape + discipline intact, not a rewrite): added the findings doc as item 0 in the read-first list (the methodological basis; "where it and §2.5 disagree on a number, the findings doc wins"); **Phase 0** gained the researched case-design discipline (open-code real frames first; 30–60 balanced cases not 200; Sean as benevolent-dictator labeler; baseline = a scored confusion matrix with **false-pass rate front and center**, never raw agreement/F1-alone; the Goodhart "don't tune cases to pass" line sharpened against the legitimate criteria-drift fork); **Phase 1** gained the motion-sight honesty (the shuffled-frames finding, contact-sheet-for-identity/style + explicit motion-proper coverage decision, DINOv2 backstop, the pencil-boil caveat); **Phase 2** replaced the provisional metric list with the calibration-against-Sean's-labels procedure + the bias-defense set + the corrected ledger + model-snapshot pinning (anima's biggest silent-regression exposure). **Why:** The critic-spine kickoff assumed eval competence that PHILOSOPHY's "empirical, not vibes" demands be grounded, not improvised — and verifying the project's own cited numbers caught three that needed fixing, which is exactly what that belief is for. ## 2026-05-31 — The Museum SHIPPED: schema + backfill + Mo + finished standalone site

**What changed:** Built the Museum capture layer end-to-end on `feature/museum-capture-layer` — the orthogonal layer that turns `runs/` evidence into a self-contained, dated, browsable static museum inside `anima/`. Split the architecture's single word "capture" into named, separately-committed mechanisms:

- **(A) Exhibit schema** ([`pipeline/museum/schema.py`](pipeline/museum/schema.py), doc [`docs/museum-exhibit-schema.md`](docs/museum-exhibit-schema.md)) — `Exhibit`/`Decision`/`Verdict` dataclasses, the `museum/{project_slug}/{run_slug}/exhibits/{id}/` tree, config-driven `derive_project_slug`. The honesty contract is **structural**: `decision.rationale` is empty + `rationale_source` null when the logs are silent, and `evidence_completeness` (rich/partial/thin) is sortable — a thin exhibit is truthful, an invented one is the template trap.
- **(C) Read-only scraper** ([`pipeline/museum/scraper.py`](pipeline/museum/scraper.py)) — `walk_runs` honestly noise-filters (logs / install runs / aborted runs, **every skip logged**) then synthesizes exhibits from `plate_verdicts.jsonl`, `bible_audit.jsonl`, Seedance `*.meta.json` (prompt+params are the artifact; video not copied), and a per-run approved-keyframe rollup (one strip, not 40 thin pages). Strictly read-only against `runs/` and the locked Bibles.
- **(E) Comparison artifact** ([`pipeline/museum/motion.py`](pipeline/museum/motion.py) + [`pipeline/museum/motion_gif.py`](pipeline/museum/motion_gif.py)) — the signature human/agent split: one exhibit per mascot motion pairing **Sean's hand-drawn B&W key sheet** (manual-left) with the **colored frames assembled into a Pillow loop GIF** (right). Locomotion (hop) loops forward; settle motions ping-pong. Aggregates all `motion-*.json` specs (so the colored-pass `idle-04` is included).
- **(D) Mo, the museum writer** ([`pipeline/agents/museum_writer.py`](pipeline/agents/museum_writer.py), preamble [`pipeline/agents/prompts/mo-museum-writer-context.md`](pipeline/agents/prompts/mo-museum-writer-context.md)) — `@register_node("museum_writer")` AgentSpec; a competent docent, not a poet. Real path narrates via Sonnet 4.6 (`invoke_museum_prose` in [`sdk_runners.py`](pipeline/agents/sdk_runners.py)); a **faithful deterministic local fallback** runs credential-free (CI-green) and never fabricates from a stubbed model. `narrate_many` batches concurrently; `--no-sonnet` forces the fallback. The committed museum carries the fallback prose; real Sonnet docent prose is a one-command upgrade (`python scripts/build_museum.py --narrate`).
- **(F) Finished renderer** ([`pipeline/museum/render.py`](pipeline/museum/render.py)) — self-contained static site (index of projects → per-project walkthrough → per-exhibit page) with a tiny in-house Markdown→HTML for Mo's prose, the comparison/plate images inline, and a decision trail (verdict score, cited `IR.*`/`AC.*` criteria, provenance). No framework, no CDN, no build step — browses by opening a file. `museum/_site/` is gitignored (regenerable); the exhibit source tree is committed.
- **Orchestrator** ([`scripts/build_museum.py`](scripts/build_museum.py)) — `--all` full backfill, `--only`/`--motion` targeted, `--narrate`/`--no-sonnet`, `--render`. Thumbnails + palette-quantizes every committed image (589M → **~9.5M**); full-res originals stay in gitignored `runs/`.

**The backfill:** **97 exhibits** — **character-bible = 84** (Cy plate verdicts across 8 bakes, the pixel→pencil register pivot, bible mutations/adds, the 6 motion comparisons), **pencil-test = 13** (10 Seedance shots + Act 1 / head-turn approved-keyframe rollups). 15 runs kept, **13 filtered** (logged: 5 logs, 6 aborted, install runs) + 2 empty-skip.

**Tests:** 207 → **230 passing** (+23 across schema/scraper/motion/motion_gif/writer/render), zero regressions. Each mechanism its own commit, test-first.

**Why:** PHILOSOPHY calls the museum core, not bolted-on ("the museum is the evidence"), and `sw-ai-pm-portfolio`'s walkthrough is a hard dependency on a `museum/` output that did not exist. This converts the heavy Cy investment from sunk cost into dated, displayable proof, and gives the portfolio its load-bearing differentiator. **What changed:** Sean's six hand-drawn motion sheets (his own pencil keys — the Phase 4 animatic) were cropped into **22 per-pose plates** via column-projection segmentation (`motion_plates/{idle-01..03, look-01..04, perch-01..04, alert-01..03, hop-01..05, sleep-01..03}.png`, mirroring sean-anchor's `head-turn-01..09` flat naming) and ingested into the **locked** mascot Bible via `bible add` with **seven new `IR.claude-mascot.motion.*` rules** (idle-breath-volume, tilt-is-whole-body, perch-weight-and-squash, alert-snap-eyes-stay-dots, hop-arc-and-gravity, sleep-ease-in, no-arms-in-motion). **Bug found + fixed:** `python -m pipeline.cli bible add ...` exited **1 silently** — the `add` subparser was registered in `__main__.py` but the dispatch switch had **no `add` branch**, so it fell through to the bare `return 1` and never called `add_to_bible` (the function itself was correct; the expression-expansion CHANGELOG's "CLI wired … add …" claim was aspirational). Added the missing dispatch branch in [`pipeline/cli/__main__.py`](pipeline/cli/__main__.py). Root cause it slipped through: `test_bible_add.py` only ever called the function directly — no test exercised the argv path. Added `test_cli_main_dispatches_bible_add` in [`tests/test_cli_bible.py`](tests/test_cli_bible.py) (invokes `main(["bible","add",...])` end-to-end, asserts rc 0 + rule landed + still locked + audit written). Bible CLI suite 21 → **22 passing**; the real ingest above was performed through `add_to_bible` directly before the fix, then the fix was verified by re-running the CLI (now prints the real dup-rule error instead of exiting silent).

**Why:** The risk-bible named motion plates as the load-bearing Act 2 gap — 0 plates, 0 `IR.*.motion.*` rules, so Em (T2) couldn't ground a motion-drift verdict. Per PHILOSOPHY the human owns timing: these are Sean's hand-drawn keys, ingested zero-drift via the audited additive path exactly like the turnaround crops. The mascot now has citable motion rules and per-pose Seedance anchors; the CLI fix makes the documented `bible add` path actually executable.

Rewrote the Cy skills-map row: `_build_plate_prompt` + `_REGISTER_CLAUSE_LIBRARY` is the prompt-construction source of truth (the five-slot register-agnostic template); `_resolve_plate_model` / `_REGISTER_MODELS` is per-register routing (NB2 editing default, NB Pro painterly-final seam, manifest override); `invoke_image_edit` is the renamed runner entry point. ## 2026-05-30 — Per-register model routing + `invoke_nb_pro` → `invoke_image_edit` rename

**What changed:** Added per-register model routing (Amendment B). `_resolve_plate_model(style_register, char_cfg, *, final=False)` in [`pipeline/agents/character_designer.py`](pipeline/agents/character_designer.py) reads a new `_REGISTER_MODELS` table: NB2 (`gemini-3.1-flash-image-preview`) for editing/generation in every register, NB Pro (`gemini-3-pro-image-preview`) reserved for painterly FINAL renders (watercolor / photoreal / 3d-rendered). A per-character manifest override (`characters.{id}.generation_model` / `final_model`) wins over the register default; `author_bible.py` passes `manifest={}`, so the register default is the safety net. `run()` resolves the editing model once and threads it through `_run_plate` → both `invoke_image_edit` calls via `model=`. Renamed `invoke_nb_pro` → `invoke_image_edit` in [`pipeline/agents/nb_pro_runner.py`](pipeline/agents/nb_pro_runner.py) (model is a parameter; the name should not assert Pro) with a `invoke_nb_pro = invoke_image_edit` deprecation alias retained; updated the import + both call sites + every test reference. Manifest gained a comment documenting the override shape. Tests: `test_resolve_plate_model_routes_by_register` (NB2 default per register; watercolor/photoreal final → Pro; pencil final stays NB2; manifest override wins; unknown register → pencil default). Suite 199 → 200.

**Why:** Cy's entire job is identity-preserving editing, and the 2026-05-30 research is decisive that NB2 holds identity better across edits, costs ~half, runs ~4× faster, and dodges NB Pro's documented multi-reference downsampling regression. The runner defaulted Cy's most consistency-sensitive work to the model currently worst at consistency. **The NB-Pro final-render path is a documented seam, not a built branch:** no Pro-routed character exists, so `_run_plate` always uses the generation model (NB2) and the `final=True` branch + the forum teams' reference-fidelity guard are deferred until a consumer exists — over-building a branch nothing exercises invites rot, and the freshness caveat (the Pro regression may be patched) means the guard's necessity must be re-verified before it's relied on. `_resolve_plate_model(..., final=True)` is implemented and unit-tested so the seam is ready when a watercolor/photoreal/3D character lands.

## 2026-05-30 — Fix: `bible iterate` reject-reason steers the prompt, not just the cache

**What changed:** Wired `reject_reason` into the emitted prompt at both points in `_run_plate` ([`pipeline/agents/character_designer.py`](pipeline/agents/character_designer.py)): the `bible iterate` plate-level `reject_reason` on the initial generate (woven into `{preserve_and_negative}` via `_build_plate_prompt`, and now also forwarded to `invoke_nb_pro` so the cache key busts), and the Pass-3 fail reasoning on the regenerate (the prompt is rebuilt with the reason rather than reusing the original `prompt_text`). Test: `test_iterate_reject_reason_reaches_emitted_prompt` calls `_run_plate` directly with a reject-carrying plate and asserts the captured prompt CONTAINS the reason — the assertion the §3 bug would have failed (it asserts on the prompt, not a changed cache key). Suite 198 → 199.

**Why:** Post-mortem §3. Before, `reject_reason` only busted the `invoke_nb_pro` cache key; `_build_skill_cmd` builds the argv from `prompt` alone, so a re-roll re-sampled the identical prompt — gambling, not steering. The drift-fix lever (the plate intent edit done by hand during the pivot) is now structural: a reject reason reaches the model. This is the difference between `iterate` fixing a drift and `iterate` re-rolling the dice.

## 2026-05-30 — Refactor: Cy plate prompts via a register-parameterized five-slot emitter

**What changed:** Generalized `_build_nb_pro_prompt` into `_build_plate_prompt` in [`pipeline/agents/character_designer.py`](pipeline/agents/character_designer.py) — the register-agnostic editing template (Amendment A; spec in [`docs/research/2026-05-30-nb2-editing-character-consistency-template.md`](docs/research/2026-05-30-nb2-editing-character-consistency-template.md)). It reads a new `_REGISTER_CLAUSE_LIBRARY` (a real dict, the six closed registers) to fill the `{identity_lock}`, `{preserve_and_negative}`, and `{style_register}` slots from the matched row; `{variation}` stays Cy's terse intent wrapped in the `ONLY CHANGE` idiom; the universal anti-text clause is appended to every register. `_build_prop_prompt` stays the isolated-object `{output_spec}` special case (now also accepting an optional `reject_reason`). `_run_plate` gained a `style_register` parameter (resolved once in `run()` from `character.yaml`) and now reads a plate-level `reject_reason` so a `bible iterate` correction reaches the prompt on the initial generate. Added the paired paragraph to [`pipeline/agents/prompts/cy-character-designer-context.md`](pipeline/agents/prompts/cy-character-designer-context.md) explaining that Cy authors only `{variation}` and `style_register` now selects the identity-lock enumeration + style token. Tests: six emitter tests (each register fills its slots; pencil keeps the full-color line; line-art forbids shading; prop path byte-identical via the emitter; unknown register falls back to pencil). Suite 192 → 198.

**Why:** Centralizing the template in the runner is the single source of truth the field report argued for, and lets Phase 3 storyboarding and Phase 5 Flo later draw from the same emitter instead of reinventing the structure. **Important — this is a deliberate prompt UPGRADE, not a no-op.** The new pencil emit is richer than the prior builder: it adds the `ONLY CHANGE` idiom, the full preserve clause (cream paper, cross-hatch, "do not render monochrome"), and a standing style token to *every* plate. That is the approved template spec — worked Example 1, the prompt that would have prevented the `focused` monochrome drift — but it IS a change. The substring tests pin the new clauses' presence, not equivalence to the old output. The first live bake on the new emitter is its validation point: adding standing prose to every prompt is the exact surface the prompt-dominance lesson warns about, with the saving grace that the added prose is anchor-reinforcing register/preserve guidance, not character re-description that competes with the anchor. If a bake shows drift traceable to the added prose, trim the clause library; don't revert the structure.

## 2026-05-30 — Fix: `bible mutate` edits rule content and keeps the schema version loadable

**What changed:** Rewrote `mutate_bible` in [`pipeline/cli/bible.py`](pipeline/cli/bible.py) to fix the two bugs the pivot surfaced (post-mortem §4). It now (1) finds the criterion whose `id == --target`, sets `criterion[--field] = --value`, re-validates the whole graph, and writes back in place via a resolved-path atomic write — no symlink/versioned-file dance; and (2) leaves the schema `version` field untouched at its current value (`1.2`), recording any `--new-version` as a separate top-level `content_version` field the loader ignores. `--new-version` is now optional. Unknown `--target` errors (rc 1) instead of silently no-opping. The audit record gains `old_value` and `content_version_from`/`_to`; the schema-conflating `criteria_version_to` field is gone. `bump_version` is no longer imported by `bible.py` (it stays in `pipeline/criteria.py` for Maya's plan/brief flow). Tests: new [`tests/test_bible_mutate.py`](tests/test_bible_mutate.py) (field-change-applied + still-loadable + content_version recorded + unknown-target errors); updated the three `test_cli_bible.py` mutate tests to the new contract. Suite 189 → 192.

**Why:** `bible mutate --new-version 1.3.0` wrote a *content* semver into the *schema*-`version` field that `validate_criteria` gates on a `1.0/1.1/1.2` allowlist, making the Bible unloadable — and separately, mutate was audit-only: it bumped the version and wrote the audit record but never applied the field change to the rule content. Decoupling content-version from schema-version is the minimal correct fix and lets the CLAUDE.md ⚠️ caution be lifted. The new `tests/test_bible_mutate.py` (with the live-manifest tripwire from the prior commit) is the coverage that was missing — a fixture-only suite stayed green while a real mutate corrupted a locked Bible. **Latent sibling bug queued, not fixed here:** Maya's `plan mutate` (`pipeline/cli/plan.py`) still calls `bump_version`, which writes into the same schema-gated `version` field — the identical break fires for any `--new-version` whose major.minor falls outside the allowlist (e.g. `1.3.0`). Recommended follow-on: apply the same decoupling to `mutate_plan`, or harden `bump_version` to refuse an off-schema version (protecting both callers).

## 2026-05-30 — Safety-net: live-manifest merged criteria must load (regression tripwire)

**What changed:** Added [`tests/test_live_manifest_criteria.py`](tests/test_live_manifest_criteria.py) — a single integration test that loads the *real* `manifest.yaml` (not a fixture), merges every Bible's `IR.*` graph via `load_all_criteria`, and asserts the merged bundle parses with zero ID collisions across `IR.*` namespaces (and that both `IR.sean.*` and `IR.claude-mascot.*` are present). Passes against the current restored state — it is the guard, not a red-to-green. Suite 188 → 189.

**Why:** This is the single test that would have caught the `bible mutate --new-version 1.3.0` schema break at commit time. The pivot session shipped an unloadable Bible with a green suite because every criteria test uses fixtures; nothing loaded the live manifest's on-disk Bibles. Landed first so the rest of the template-emitter follow-on has the net. If this test ever goes red, stop and fix the on-disk criteria before proceeding.

## 2026-05-30 — Doc safety: defuse the `bible mutate --new-version` landmine in CLAUDE.md

**What changed:** The Key Commands section of [`CLAUDE.md`](CLAUDE.md) showed the canonical `bible mutate` example ending in `--new-version 1.3.0` — the exact invocation that wrote an unloadable schema version and broke the claude-mascot Bible during the pivot (see [`docs/anima-test-runs/2026-05-30-claude-mascot-pencil-register-pivot.md`](docs/anima-test-runs/2026-05-30-claude-mascot-pencil-register-pivot.md) §4). Removed `--new-version` from the example and added a loud inline ⚠️ KNOWN BUG caution explaining the content-semver-vs-schema-version conflation and pointing at the post-mortem. Documentation only — the underlying tool bug remains for the template-emitter follow-on to fix (split content-version from schema-version).

**Why:** The wrap commit added a bug *note* on the Cy skills-map row but left the broken example standing in the manual with no warning. CLAUDE.md is what every session reads first; a copy-pasteable command that corrupts a locked Bible is a landmine for the next session. Defusing the example is independent of (and more urgent than) the code fix.

## 2026-05-30 — claude-mascot pencil-register pivot

**What changed:** Pivoted the claude-mascot character from `pixel-art-8bit` to `pencil-test-colored` and re-authored its Bible against real multi-view reference art, baked on NB2. Per-phase:

- **Phase 1 — retire the pixel Bible.** `git mv` the whole locked pixel-art-8bit Bible to [`characters/_archive/claude-mascot-pixel-art-8bit/`](characters/_archive/claude-mascot-pixel-art-8bit/) (history preserved) with a README recording the failure; flipped `manifest.yaml` `characters.claude-mascot.style_register` → `pencil-test-colored`. `criteria_sources` still lists the mascot criteria path; `load_all_criteria` skips the now-absent file non-fatally until Phase 3 re-creates it.
- **Phase 2 — stage source material.** Re-scaffolded `characters/claude-mascot/` (`bible init`) and staged the real reference art: `claude-mascot.png` → `anchor.png` (C-B ¾ hero portrait, the identity anchor), `claude-mascot-turnaround.png` → `source-refs/turnaround-c1.png` (the load-bearing five-view sheet — FRONT/¾FRONT/SIDE/¾BACK/BACK on one horizon line — that closes the angle-expansion gap), `sean-with-claude-mascot.png` → `source-refs/sean-with-claude-mascot.png` (A-7 relationship/scale + Act 2 two-character continuity ground-truth). Authored `source-refs/notes.md` with the box-creature form, proportions (≈1:1.2 box, shoulder-companion scale), register, and the trait-lock token.
- **Phase 3.5 — route the editing-model default to NB2.** Flipped `invoke_nb_pro`'s `model` default from `gemini-3-pro-image-preview` (NB Pro) to `gemini-3.1-flash-image-preview` (NB2) in [`pipeline/agents/nb_pro_runner.py`](pipeline/agents/nb_pro_runner.py), with a backing test (`test_default_model_is_nb2_flash`). `_run_plate` calls `invoke_nb_pro` without a `model=` arg, so this is what routes the mascot bake to NB2. One-line default flip only — `_build_nb_pro_prompt` is untouched, so it cannot bake in a prompt shape the follow-on template-emitter refactor reworks. Per-register manifest routing + the `invoke_image_edit` rename stay deferred to that follow-on (Amendments A/B). Suite 187 → 188.

**Why (Phase 3.5):** Cy's entire job is identity-preserving editing, and the 2026-05-30 research is decisive that NB2 holds identity better across edits, costs ~half, runs ~4× faster, and dodges NB Pro's documented multi-reference downsampling regression. `invoke_nb_pro` defaulted to NB Pro — backwards for this work. Freshness caveat: the regression is operational and may be patched; re-verify before relying on a guard, but NB2's cost/speed/identity edge holds regardless.

- **Phase 3 — re-author + approve the Bible.** Full Cy authoring run (Opus Pass 1, ~790s wall) re-authored `IR.claude-mascot.*` in the pencil-test register: 6-entry palette (terracotta body `#C77C52`, cream paper `#F2E6CC`, warm-graphite line `#3D3530`, etc.), rounded-box ~1:1.2 proportions, and 13 identity rules across anatomy / face / palette / pose / proportion / style. Register-purity holds — the only "pixel" mentions are deliberate contrasts with the retired version; zero pixel-art rules authored. Sean reviewed the tear sheet and approved (`locked=true`). Two review outcomes folded in: (1) Sean confirmed the C-1 SIDE-view circular "swirl" is the **ear/arm nub seen end-on**, not construction or a new feature — captured as a dedicated rule `IR.claude-mascot.anatomy.nub-side-view-endcap` (also forbids inventing spurious face discs) and Cy's hedge resolved; (2) Cy chose to **ingest** the five turnaround views as crops from the real C-1 sheet (zero-drift) and **generate** only the two expressions — a higher-fidelity plate strategy than the kickoff's generate-all. Note: a `RuntimeError: aclose()` async-generator teardown warning from claude-agent-sdk on Python 3.14 is noisy but harmless (Pass 1 wrote all artifacts); the first run's buffered-stdout variant lost output to that teardown, fixed by running unbuffered.

- **Phase 4 — bake the plates on NB2.** Authored `source-refs/turnaround-c1.regions.json` (five fractional crop boxes, derived by detecting the figure columns in the C-1 sheet) so the ingest `#region:` crops resolve — without it the runner copies the whole sheet and flags `region_not_cropped`. Plates-only bake on NB2 produced five clean turnaround crops of Sean's real art (on-model by construction; Sean: "perfect") plus two generated expressions. First-pass expressions drifted (NB2 enlarged the dot eyes into glossy cartoon eyes, and `neutral` grew a hair tuft + drooping nubs), so: added the standing invariant `IR.claude-mascot.anatomy.no-hair` (audited `bible mutate --force --actor sean`, criteria → v1.3.0, 14 rules) and re-rolled both expressions with targeted anti-drift negatives in the plate intent (small dot eyes, no hair, horizontal nubs). Re-roll landed: `neutral` pass, `curious` borderline, both on-model. DINOv2 verdict trails persisted to the bake run dirs. Sean reviewed and approved the full plate set.

- **Post-mortem.** Wrote [`docs/anima-test-runs/2026-05-30-claude-mascot-pencil-register-pivot.md`](docs/anima-test-runs/2026-05-30-claude-mascot-pencil-register-pivot.md) — the field report for this session in the voice of the 2026-05-28 end-to-end report. Covers the four off-happy-path failures (the buffered-log 535s kill on Python 3.14 / claude-agent-sdk async-generator teardown; the missing C-1 regions sidecar that made turnarounds full-sheet copies; the expression eye/hair drift + the discovery that `bible iterate`'s reject_reason never reaches the NB2 prompt; the `bible mutate --new-version` schema-version break), Cy's positive deviation (ingest-crop the turnarounds rather than generate), the two-character first light, the structural lessons, and how to proceed (expand expressions/poses for both Bibles next; two tool bugs + one missing integration test for the follow-on; the cross-character continuity audit as the scoped next session).

- **Phase 5 — two-character first light (exploratory).** First time anima loaded two real Bibles into one scene. Confirmed `load_all_criteria` merges sean-anchor + claude-mascot into one `CriteriaBundle` — 36 entries (22 `IR.sean.*` + 14 `IR.claude-mascot.*`), zero ID collisions. Generated one two-character frame (Sean + mascot on shoulder, NB2) through the editing-template storyboard variant, referencing both anchors + A-7; continuity held against A-7 (Sean recognizable + stylus-in-right-hand, mascot is the box-creature + no hair, shoulder-companion scale, one consistent register). Wrote [`docs/anima-test-runs/2026-05-30-two-character-first-light.md`](docs/anima-test-runs/2026-05-30-two-character-first-light.md) scoping what a real cross-character continuity audit needs (per-character IR loading into one verdict, a relative-scale ratio rule, occlusion / who-occludes-whom, a shared-register check, pairing-placement invariants) — `continuity_audit.py` CC01–CC08 are still Sean/Act-1-hardcoded. **The continuity system was deliberately NOT built this session.**

**Why (Phase 4):** A bare `bible iterate` re-samples with the identical prompt — its `reject_reason` only busts the `invoke_nb_pro` cache key, it does not reach the NB2 prompt — so steering a drift fix required editing the plate intent. The no-hair drift is exactly the "generator reads the box-top as a head and reaches for hair" failure worth locking as an enforceable, Em-citable rule rather than fixing only in a one-off prompt.

- **Phase 4 follow-up — schema-version fix.** `bible mutate --new-version 1.3.0` wrote `1.3.0` into the criteria `version` field, which is the *schema* version `validate_criteria` gates on an allowlist (`1.0`/`1.1`/`1.2`) — so the mutated file failed to load (`unsupported criteria schema version: 1.3.0`). The 14-rule content is valid 1.2 (adding a rule needs no schema bump). Restored `acceptance_criteria.json` to a plain regular file at `version: "1.2"` (matching sean-anchor and Cy's original write), removed the symlink + versioned file. **Latent tool bug noted for the follow-on:** `bible mutate` conflates a content semver (`--new-version`) with the schema-version field and will break any locked Bible it touches until that's split.

**Why:** The pixel mascot failed on a *reference gap* (single flat anchor → NB Pro invented a standing biped for turnarounds; 2026-05-29 bake post-mortem §6) and Sean won't ship a pixelated mascot. The pencil-test version has a real five-view turnaround sheet that closes the gap, lives in sean-anchor's register, and is the actual Act 2 shoulder companion. The pixel Bible is kept as register-vocabulary validation evidence (the schema was clean; generation failed). Pixel cross-register validation deferred to a future 16BitFit-humanoid pass.

## 2026-05-30 — Research + plan: register-agnostic NB2 editing-prompt template

**What changed:** Added two docs, no code. (1) [`docs/research/2026-05-30-nb2-editing-character-consistency-template.md`](docs/research/2026-05-30-nb2-editing-character-consistency-template.md) — current (mid-2026) research on NB2's *editing* mode (image+text identity preservation, distinct from generation), plus the headline artifact: a register-agnostic five-slot editing-prompt template (`{identity_lock}` / `{variation}` / `{preserve_and_negative}` / `{style_register}` / `{output_spec}`) with a per-register clause library, three worked examples in three registers (pencil-test, pixel-art, line-art/anime), and a storyboard variant. Builds on (does not repeat) the 2026-05-30 pixel/angle-expansion research. (2) [`docs/2026-05-30-claude-mascot-pencil-register-pivot-kickoff-amendments.md`](docs/2026-05-30-claude-mascot-pencil-register-pivot-kickoff-amendments.md) — wires the template into Cy as a plan for the next session: refactor `_build_nb_pro_prompt` into a register-parameterized template emitter (Cy still authors only `{variation}`), flip the editing-model default to **NB2** with a per-register split (NB Pro reserved for painterly/watercolor/3D finals, guarded), and recognize the template as a Phase-2/3/5 primitive (Cy plates, storyboard shot lists, Flo keyframes).

**Why:** Cy's plate prompting was tuned ad hoc and skewed pencil-test; Sean wanted a rock-solid register-agnostic editing template that serves any 2D style and both Bible authoring and storyboarding. The research surfaced one behavior contradiction worth acting on: editing/consistency work — Cy's whole job — should route to NB2, but `invoke_nb_pro` currently defaults to `gemini-3-pro-image-preview`, which carries a documented multi-reference downsampling regression since the 3.1 launch. Two forks (template wiring; model routing) were decided by Sean this session: refactor the runner builder, per-register split. No production code touched — the next session implements. Also folded a two-paragraph pointer into [`docs/2026-05-30-claude-mascot-pencil-register-pivot-kickoff.md`](docs/2026-05-30-claude-mascot-pencil-register-pivot-kickoff.md) so the implementing session reads both companion docs, routes the Phase 4 bake to NB2, and uses the storyboard variant for the Phase 5 two-character frame.

Covers each phase's failure/finding (the prop over-generalization, the bake-vs-approve conflict that would have erased the approval and never ran, the `focused` prompt-dominance recurrence, the mascot reference gap, the DINOv2 promotion the data killed, the Pass-1 retry), the structural lessons (organizing lesson: *the mechanism is a proposal, not a verdict*), and how to proceed (mascot dedicated pass, trim the remaining expression prompts, per-view hard gate, identity tuning, Em case 7). ## 2026-05-29 — Session: post-fidelity-fix production + hardening (summary)

Eight commits across nine phases, 176 → 187 tests green throughout. The arc: fix the last mechanism bug, finish the sean-anchor production bake the fidelity fix deferred, and harden the gate + runner. Phase-by-phase entries follow below; the through-line:

- **Phase 1** — prop plates are isolated objects (no anchor, no identity gate, no caption); validated live in Phase 5's `props/stylus.png`.
- **Phase 2** — sean-anchor body turnarounds use Sean's hand-trimmed crops; head crops tightened.
- **Phase 4** — added the **plates-only bake mode** (a locked Bible is never re-authored — the capability the "approve → bake" flow assumed), propagated full-color into the sibling docs, and **approved** the sean-anchor Bible (22 rules, v1.2, locked).
- **Phase 5** — **baked the sean-anchor production plates** against the approved Bible; recognizably-Sean full-color set (two plates re-rolled: `focused` monochrome→color, `stylus` metallic→pencil).
- **Phase 6** — claude-mascot re-bake **held**: the crouched-octopus anchor can't support standing body turnarounds (reference gap, documented for a dedicated pass).
- **Phase 7** — installed the **DINOv2 similarity tier** + a cross-register regression eval; kept the gate **record-only** (the data showed a blanket hard threshold would false-reject good plates).
- **Phase 8** — **Cy Pass-1 retry-on-parse-failure** (auto-heal transient Opus 4.8 malformations within the 3-call budget).

Out of scope / deferred this session: the mascot dedicated pass (Phase 6 finding), a per-view-reference hard gate (Phase 7 finding), Em's closing-the-loop case 7 (still xfailed), making the repo public.

## 2026-05-29 — Phase 8: Cy Pass-1 retry-on-parse-failure (auto-heal transient Opus 4.8 malformations)

**What changed:** `_author_pass1` ([`pipeline/agents/character_designer.py`](pipeline/agents/character_designer.py)) now retries a transient malformed Opus emission within Cy's three-call Pass-1 budget instead of stubbing on the first bad output. The 2026-05-28 mascot bake hit exactly this — Opus 4.8 emitted unparseable narration/truncation, the loud guard fired correctly, but it required a human re-run.

- **Retry only the transient case.** A retry fires when the SDK *ran* but returned empty or unparseable text (`_pass1_stub`). It does **not** fire for a missing SDK (`stub_fallback=True` — deterministic, retrying can't help; one call then the loud stub) or a contract violation (parseable JSON missing required keys — `_parse_pass1_envelope` raises `ValueError`, which propagates as a real rejection). Budget = `_PASS1_CALL_CEILING` (3).
- **Tests** (2 added → 187 green): a first-call malformed + second-call clean emission yields a *real* Bible (no stub, criteria carry the real IR ids) in exactly 2 calls; a missing-SDK stub is *not* retried (1 call, loud stub).

**Why:** The loud guard turned a silent stub-ship into a visible failure; this turns the common transient case (Opus 4.8's chattier disposition occasionally malforming a large structured emission) into an automatic recovery, so a one-off bad emission no longer costs a human re-run. The guard still fires when all three attempts fail.

## 2026-05-29 — Phase 7: DINOv2 similarity tier + regression eval; gate stays record-only (a hard gate isn't safe yet)

**What changed:** Installed the embedding tier the gate's ladder was built for, added a cross-register regression eval, and — after measuring — kept the gate record-only rather than promoting it to a hard pre-Gemini reject (Sean's call on the data).

- **DINOv2 tier active.** `pip install torch torchvision transformers` into `.venv`. The ladder in [`pipeline/agents/similarity_gate.py`](pipeline/agents/similarity_gate.py) auto-selects DINOv2 (`facebook/dinov2-small`) with no code change. **Gotcha found + documented:** transformers 5.x's `AutoImageProcessor` needs **torchvision** — without it the DINOv2 rung raises during `from_pretrained` and *silently* falls back to PIL (the `SimilarityResult.method` label is the tell). Updated the install hint accordingly.
- **Regression eval** ([`evals/similarity-gate/`](evals/similarity-gate/) — README + 6 fixtures; executable guard in `tests/test_similarity_gate.py::test_dinov2_regression_recovered_above_drifted`, skipped without torch). DINOv2 ranks the recovered plate above the drifted plate vs the anchor on **both** registers — sean 0.838 > 0.755, mascot 0.858 > 0.715 — including the mascot register where the PIL tier *inverted*.
- **Gate stays RECORD-ONLY — the planned hard-gate promotion is unsafe.** Re-scoring the sean-anchor production bake with DINOv2 showed the drifted references (0.715–0.755) sit *inside* the good-plate range (head-back 0.695, neutral 0.722, surprised 0.740 …). A single blanket threshold against the one front anchor can't separate identity drift from legitimate view/expression variation: a drift-catching threshold false-rejects good plates; a safe one catches nothing. DINOv2 separates recovered-from-drifted only at the *same view*. A trustworthy hard gate needs **per-view references** — future work. Documented in the gate docstring + the eval README. Prop exemption intact.
- **Tests** now tier-deterministic: PIL-specific assertions use a `force_pil` fixture (disable the embedding rungs) so they don't depend on whether torch is installed; the method-label assertion relaxed to "names a known tier." 185 green (182 + the 2 regression params + 1 PIL-label test) with torch present; the suite also stays green without torch (regression skips, force_pil holds).

**Why:** The honest result beat the planned one. Installing DINOv2 made the *scores* trustworthy and the regression eval meaningful, but the data proved a blanket hard gate would harm good plates more than it catches drift. Shipping the tier + eval + the documented "why not a hard gate" is the correct landing; the human/visual gate remains the arbiter, exactly as the engine truth says.

## 2026-05-29 — Phase 6: claude-mascot re-bake held for a dedicated pass (reference gap documented)

**What changed:** Ran the full claude-mascot plates-only bake (locked Bible → no Opus call, so no transient-stub risk — the limit that capped the 2026-05-28 mascot bake to one plate). All 8 plates ran. Sean reviewed and chose to **hold** the commit; the working-tree plates were reverted (committed mascot Bible untouched) and the result documented for a dedicated pass.

- **Mixed result, split by plate type.** The fixed mechanism recovers the orange pixel-octopus on **front / expression / profile** views (`contemplative` is a clean octopus with stub legs; `surprised` is the octopus but on a black background; `body-profile-right` reads as the creature). It does **not** recover the **standing body turnarounds** (`body-3quarter`, `body-back` → standing chibi-humanoids) — categorically better than the pre-fix "every plate a generic humanoid that passed," but still drifting on those two.
- **Root cause is a reference gap, not prompt-dominance.** The anchor is a tiny *crouched* octopus with no standing pose, so NB Pro invents a standing biped for a "3/4 body" or "back" turnaround. Trimming the prompt (the sean-anchor `focused` fix) won't recover it — the information isn't in the single anchor. This is a Bible-silence problem.
- **Documented, not committed.** Full finding + labelled evidence (anchor, the good octopus, the humanoid drifters, the contact sheet, the verdict trail) in [`docs/anima-test-runs/2026-05-29-mascot-rebake-hold/`](docs/anima-test-runs/2026-05-29-mascot-rebake-hold/). Recommendation for the dedicated pass: reconsider whether a crouched-octopus needs standing turnarounds at all, add a true standing/multi-angle reference, or train a character LoRA on the octopus form; cheap re-rolls available for `surprised` (bg) and `head-front` (lost snout).

**Why:** Forcing standing turnarounds onto a minimal crouched-creature anchor produces humanoid drift the mechanism can't fix from references alone. Better to ship the sean-anchor win, document the mascot reference gap honestly, and give the octopus its own pass than to commit half-drifted plates. The committed mascot Bible (rules + plan) is unchanged. 182 tests green.

## 2026-05-29 — Phase 5: bake the sean-anchor production plates against the approved Bible

**What changed:** Ran the first production plate bake against the locked full-color Bible — via the new plates-only path, so Pass 1 was skipped entirely (no Opus call, no transient-stub risk). 24 plates regenerated into `characters/sean-anchor/{turnarounds,expressions,props,motion_plates}/`.

- **The mechanism + prop fix validated live.** `props/stylus.png` came back a clean isolated object (no figure, no caption) — the Phase 1 fix working under real NB Pro. The generated expression + head plates recovered identity in full color (blonde, blue eyes, warm skin, navy tee, construction lines, cross-hatch) — recognizably Sean, a categorical improvement over the pre-fix monochrome "different person."
- **Two plates re-rolled at Sean's call.** `expressions/focused.png` first baked **monochrome** (the plate's leftover verbose prompt — "no explicit skin tone", heavy "warm graphite #3D3530" — fought the runner's "keep full color" framing and won; the reject-reason feedback loop amplified it). Trimming the plan prompt to a short expression-intent let the runner's anchor framing drive: re-roll came back full color, similarity 0.23 → **0.81**. `props/stylus.png` re-rolled in the pencil-test line register (was metallic-realistic) by naming the register in the plate intent — isolated-object framing preserved. Both via a surgical single-plate re-run (changed prompt → cache-bust) so the passing plates were untouched.
- **Housekeeping.** Deleted the stale `turnarounds/body-front.png` (dropped from the plan in Phase 2). Patched `plate_verdicts.jsonl` for the two re-rolls. The "12 human-gated" plates were 10 ingests (Sean's own crops + line-art motion frames — Gemini-skeptical of small crops, not real failures) + the 2 re-rolled.
- **Known item logged** (`cy-confidence-notes.md` §6): the generated faces lean a touch more realistic than the round-cartoon anchor — a stylization-amount drift, not identity drift. Shipped knowingly; flagged for a future tuning pass (prompt nudge or a round-anchor LoRA).

**Why:** This is the bake the whole fidelity arc was building toward — the approved rules rendered into a recognizable, full-color, in-register plate set. The plates-only path meant it ran against the approved Bible without re-authoring it. 182 tests green.

## 2026-05-29 — Phase 4: full-color doc consistency pass + approve the sean-anchor Bible

**What changed:** Propagated the full-color decision into the Bible's sibling docs (commit 3 only updated `acceptance_criteria.json`), then locked the Bible.

- **`character.yaml`** — palette went 4 → 8 colors, adding warm skin `#F0DFCB`, dirty-blonde hair `#AD9468`, warm-gray sneakers `#7E807B`, blue eyes `#4A6D8C`, and dropping the "no dedicated skin color — paper shows through" language from cream_paper. Proportions converted to the renderer's canonical keys (`head_to_body` / `shoulder_to_hip` / `notes`) so the tear sheet renders them instead of "(unset)". `flux_lora_seed_plates` dropped the retired `turnarounds/body-front.png` (→ `body-3quarter`). The inline confidence summary's axis 5 flipped from "skin tone intentionally absent" to "full color is canonical; the skin/eye hexes are sampled, eyeball them."
- **`risk-bible.md`** — the three monochrome passages ("palette locked at four steps; skin tone intentionally absent", "locked at four colors and excludes skin tone", "any departure from the four-step palette") rewritten to the full-color limited palette. The view-source paragraph corrected to match the committed plan: bodies ingest Sean's hand-trimmed `source-refs/body-turnarounds/` crops; head-front/3quarter/profile-left are colored `#region` crops; profile-right + back are generated.
- **`cy-confidence-notes.md`** — section 5 rewritten (full color canonical; the remaining hedge is hex *precision*, not skin *presence*). Section 1 corrected: head turnarounds source from the colored turnaround sheet, not the line-art head-turn frames.
- **Approved.** `pipeline bible approve` flipped `acceptance_criteria.json` to `locked: true` (22 rules, v1.2). Sean confirmed the palette hexes (incl. the two estimates, skin `#F0DFCB` and eyes `#4A6D8C`). The lock is also what routes the Phase 5 bake to plates-only.

**Why:** A reviewer reading `bible show` (or any downstream consumer reading the sibling docs) would have seen a 4-color monochrome palette that directly contradicted the locked full-color rules. Locking the Bible on inconsistent docs would have shipped that contradiction. 182 tests green.

## 2026-05-29 — Phase 4a: plates-only bake mode — regenerate plates without re-authoring an approved Bible

**What changed:** Added the missing capability the "approve → bake" flow assumes. `CharacterDesignerNode.run` always ran Pass 1 (Opus re-authors the whole envelope — `character.yaml`, `acceptance_criteria.json` with `locked: false`, risk-bible, confidence-notes, **and `plate_generation_plan.json`**). So baking an *approved* Bible via `author_bible.py` would have overwritten the locked rules AND the hand-curated plate plan (the trimmed stylus + Sean's manual body-turnaround crops). The plan's own invariant — "approved rules (locked: true) are not touched by a bake" — had no enforcement.

- **`run()` now branches** ([`pipeline/agents/character_designer.py`](pipeline/agents/character_designer.py)). `_resolve_plates_only(ctx, character_dir)` returns True when `ctx.inputs['plates_only']` is set OR the on-disk `acceptance_criteria.json` is `locked: true` (the auto-detect is the safety net — an approved Bible is never silently re-authored). When True, `_load_existing_bible` reads `character.yaml` + `acceptance_criteria.json` (ir_entries) + `plate_generation_plan.json` from disk and Passes 2+3 run against them; **none of the Pass-1 artifacts are rewritten**. When False, the existing authoring path runs (now extracted to `_author_pass1`).
- **`_load_existing_bible` fails loudly** if the Bible was never authored (no criteria or no plan) — a plates-only bake has nothing to bake against.
- **`scripts/author_bible.py --plates-only`** plumbs the flag through; the intro line names the mode. A locked criteria auto-routes even without the flag.
- **Tests** (3 added → 182 green): plates-only skips Opus and leaves the locked criteria byte-for-byte unchanged while still generating plates; a locked criteria auto-routes to plates-only with no flag; a plates-only request against an un-authored Bible raises.

**Why:** The director approves the rules, then the plates are baked *against* those approved rules — not re-authored each time. Without this, Phase 5 would have destroyed Phases 1, 2, and 4 on the first bake. The locked-criteria auto-detect makes the protection structural, not a flag you have to remember.

## 2026-05-29 — Phase 2: body turnarounds use Sean's hand-trimmed crops; head crops tightened

**What changed:** Finalized the sean-anchor turnaround source plates. The committed `#region` crop mechanism worked, but two boxes needed work and Sean elected to hand-crop the bodies.

- **Body turnarounds now ingest Sean's manual crops.** The 4 body plates (`body-3quarter`, `body-profile-left`, `body-profile-right`, `body-back`) ingest hand-trimmed PNGs from the new [`characters/sean-anchor/source-refs/body-turnarounds/`](characters/sean-anchor/source-refs/body-turnarounds/) — one clean figure each, no neighbor bleed. The top-row sheet has no distinct *front* body pose (it's front-ish / profile-L / profile-R / back), so the old `body-front` plate is **dropped** and `body-profile-left` is **added**; the leftmost near-front figure is the canonical `body-3quarter`. cites_identity_rules migrated to match (front-pose costume/proportion rules → body-3quarter; jaw-angular → both profiles).
- **The "(A-2)" production label is trimmed off `body-3quarter`.** Sean's crop kept it; per his call it's shaved off the left edge (17% / 134px) so the canonical reference plate ships clean like the other three — the exact annotation Phase 2 set out to remove.
- **Head crops keep the `#region` mechanism, head-front box tightened.** [`turnaround-1.regions.json`](characters/sean-anchor/source-refs/turnaround-1.regions.json) `head-front` top edge nudged `0.64 → 0.66` to drop a sliver of the body-row feet; `head-3quarter` and `head-profile` unchanged (clean). The now-unused `body-*` region boxes were retired from the sidecar (bodies use manual crops).

**Why:** The engine truth is a visual one — Sean eyeballed the 7 candidate crops and chose to hand-crop the bodies for framing he was happy with, keeping the deterministic head crops. The result is a clean, label-free turnaround source set for the Phase 5 bake. 179 tests green (no code-behavior change; data + assets).

## 2026-05-29 — Phase 1: prop plates are isolated objects (no anchor, no identity gate, no caption)

**What changed:** Taught Cy's runner that a prop plate is a distinct class from a character plate. The 2026-05-29 fidelity fix made the runner inject `anchor.png` unconditionally and frame every plate around "match Image 1 exactly" — correct for turnarounds/expressions, **wrong for props**. The re-baked `props/stylus.png` rendered the full character with a stylus floating beside an empty-gripping hand, because the full-body anchor told NB Pro to draw the whole person.

- **Prop-plate predicate.** Added `_PROP_PLATE_DIRS = {"props"}` + `_is_prop_plate(plate)` (target_path under `props/`) in [`pipeline/agents/character_designer.py`](pipeline/agents/character_designer.py), mirroring `_GENERATED_PLATE_DIRS`.
- **No anchor injection for props.** `_resolve_generate_references` now returns a 3-tuple `(refs, has_pose_ref, is_prop)`; for prop plates it skips the unconditional anchor and drops any anchor Opus named, keeping only genuine source-ref/external object refs (the stylus has none → empty list — a pure text-to-image isolated-object render).
- **Isolated-object prompt.** New `_build_prop_prompt` frames the generation as an isolated object on cream paper, explicitly forbidding any person/character/hand/body/figure AND any text/caption/label/annotation. `_run_plate` branches prop → `_build_prop_prompt`, else the existing character `_build_nb_pro_prompt`.
- **Prop plates exempt from the Pass-2.5 anchor-similarity reject.** An isolated object scored against the full-character anchor always lands near zero. `_score_plate_identity(..., is_prop=True)` still records the score (audit-trail completeness) but marks `similarity_gate: "record-only (prop plate — not identity-scored)"` and never sets the below-threshold reject flag.
- **Trimmed the stylus plate prompt.** [`characters/sean-anchor/plate_generation_plan.json`](characters/sean-anchor/plate_generation_plan.json) `props/stylus.png` prompt is now a short object-intent only ("a single working-illustrator's stylus: straight cylindrical barrel ~14cm…"); the long meta-prose that NB Pro rendered as handwritten captions (post-mortem §3b) is gone, and `reference_images` is empty (the runner owns reference policy).
- **Tests.** 3 added to [`tests/test_character_designer.py`](tests/test_character_designer.py): a `props/*` plate gets an anchor-free ref list (and is_prop=True) while a character plate keeps the anchor; the prop prompt carries the no-figure + no-text clauses; a prop plate that scores below threshold is record-only with no `similarity_flag`. **179 tests green** (176 baseline + 3).

**Why:** The fidelity fix correctly made the runner the source of truth for character identity, but "every plate is the character" over-generalized — an object plate is not a character and must not be conditioned on, or scored against, the full-body anchor. This restores the stylus as a clean isolated-object reference without weakening the identity grounding that character plates depend on.

## 2026-05-29 — Session writeup: the visual-fidelity fix, end to end
