## 2026-05-29 — Commit 3b: mascot cross-register validation + a documented similarity-gate blind spot

**What changed:** Validated that the fidelity mechanism generalizes to the pixel-art-8bit register (claude-mascot), and documented an empirically-discovered limitation of the PIL similarity tier.

- **Mechanism generalizes (visual gate).** Ran one mascot generate plate (`turnarounds/head-front.png`) through the exact commit-1 code path against live NB Pro. The result is recognizably the anchor's orange pixel-octopus — blocky lozenge, dot eyes, stub legs, orange palette — **not** the pre-fix generic chibi humanoid. Evidence: `docs/anima-test-runs/2026-05-29-phase1-rebake-recovery/recovered-mascot-head-front.png` vs `mascot-anchor.png`. (Minor AA on diagonals — a Pass-3 register-purity nit, not identity drift.)
- **Similarity-gate blind spot (honest finding).** The PIL-perceptual tier **inverted** on the mascot: recovered plate 0.460 vs drifted plate 0.571 — it ranked the correct plate below the wrong one. Cause: the global color-histogram/luma metric is scale/background-sensitive, and the mascot anchor is a tiny creature on a mostly-white field while the recovered plate fills the frame. On sean-anchor (consistent full-figure framing) the ordering was correct (0.564 vs 0.468). The PIL tier is a useful severe-drift detector for consistent-framing characters but is **not reliable for tiny-subject/variable-crop registers** — the human/visual gate is the arbiter there, and the DINOv2 tier (already preferred in the ladder) is the real fix. Documented as a KNOWN BLIND SPOT in `similarity_gate.py`; do not promote the PIL tier to a hard gate for pixel-art/mascot characters.
- **Transient Pass-1 stub, loud guard worked.** The first full mascot scratch re-bake stubbed at Pass-1 and the commit-2b/2c loud-fail guard fired (no silent ship). A raw capture of the same call parsed cleanly (452s, all five keys), so it was a transient malformed Opus 4.8 emission, not a parser gap. Follow-up logged (not done): have Cy retry Pass-1 on parse failure within the three-call budget so transient malformations auto-recover.
- Full finding: `docs/anima-test-runs/2026-05-29-phase1-rebake-recovery/mascot-cross-register-finding.md`. 176 tests green (no code-behavior change; docstring + docs).

**Why:** The cross-register check is what proves the fix is structural, not a sean-anchor fluke — and it surfaced an honest limitation of the cheap gate that future sessions need to know before trusting its number on a mascot-like character. Better to name the blind spot than to let a misleading 0.46-vs-0.57 read like the fix regressed.

## 2026-05-29 — Commit 3 (Phase 4): full-color rule port + #region crop fix + register-consistency repoint

**What changed:** The Phase-4 fixes the post-mortem reserved for "after the winning model is known" (NB Pro confirmed — Track B not needed). Three things, all against the locked sean-anchor Bible, left `locked: false` for Sean's re-approval (propose, not decide). 176 tests green (172 + 4 crop tests).

- **Full-color rule port (decision e).** Hand-ported the locked Bible's rule graph to full-color, using the Opus-4.8 re-bake as the color reference. Renamed the two semantically-wrong palette rules — `palette.four-step-pencil-test-vocabulary` → `palette.full-color-pencil-test-vocabulary` (now lists cream paper #F2E6CC, graphite line #3D3530, light warm skin #F0DFCB, dirty-blonde hair #AD9468, navy tee #243044, cool-gray jeans #5C6471, warm-gray sneakers #7E807B, blue eyes) and `palette.no-explicit-skin-tone` → `palette.warm-skin-tone` (which *reverses* the old "skin is bare paper" rule — full-color is canonical). Added `IR.sean.hair.dirty-blonde-color` and `IR.sean.face.blue-eyes`. Skin hex #F0DFCB was *sampled from the recovered neutral plate*, not invented. Plate cites updated to the renamed ids + the new color rules. 20 → 22 rules; all cites resolve; schema-valid.
- **`#region` crop bug fixed (code, TDD).** The ingest path split off and *ignored* the `#region:NAME` suffix, copying the whole 2400×1792 sheet (post-mortem §2.1 — body turnarounds were byte-identical full-sheet copies). New `_region_box` + `_crop_region` read a `<sheet>.regions.json` sidecar (fractional or pixel boxes) and crop; when a region can't be mapped, the runner copies the whole sheet **and flags `region_not_cropped`** rather than silently shipping a wrong crop. Authored `source-refs/turnaround-1.regions.json` with 7 boxes (4 colored body views, 3 colored head views), visually verified (evidence in `docs/anima-test-runs/2026-05-29-phase4-crop-fix/`).
- **Register-consistency repoint.** `turnaround-1.png` is itself full-color, so the head turnarounds no longer ingest line-art head-turn *motion* frames (the register inconsistency, §2.1). Repointed `head-front` / `head-3quarter` / `head-profile-left` to colored `#region` crops of `turnaround-1`, and `head-profile-right` to `generate` (full-color mirror via the fixed mechanism). The line-art head-turn frames remain where they belong — `motion_plates/`.
- **4 new tests** (`tests/test_region_crop.py`): fractional sidecar read, no-sidecar → None, fractional crop correctness, unmappable → False (caller flags).
- **Note on plate regeneration:** the locked Bible's on-disk plate PNGs are *not* regenerated in this commit — they're pending Sean's review of the ported rules + repointed plan, then a final bake/iterate (which now works end-to-end). The crop fix is proven on the real sheet via the preserved evidence crops.

**Why:** Closes Phase 4 of the fidelity fix. The full-color port makes the rule graph say what the anchor actually shows; the crop fix makes turnarounds real crops instead of full-sheet copies; the repoint makes the turnaround set register-consistent. Left unlocked because the director approves the Bible — Cy/the-fix proposes.

## 2026-05-29 — Commit 2c: robust JSON-envelope parser (Opus 4.8 narrates around the fence) + accurate stub detection

**What changed:** The second live re-bake (now under the 1800s timeout) stubbed *again* — but this time it returned in **329s, exit 0, 26KB of text**, so it wasn't a timeout. Captured the raw Opus 4.8 Pass-1 output and found the real cause: **Opus 4.8 wraps the JSON envelope in conversational prose** ("I'm Cy, authoring Pass 1… Here is the Pass 1 envelope:" before the ` ```json ` fence, and authoring notes after it). Cy's `_CODE_FENCE_RE` was anchored to the whole string (`^…$`), so prose around the fence broke the match → `json.loads` on the whole blob failed → silent synthetic stub. The Opus 4.8 "honesty/narration" disposition is the trigger; 4.7 emitted a bare fence.

- **Robust `_parse_json_envelope` (`character_designer.py`).** Three-rung ladder: (1) the first ` ```json ``` ` fenced block found *anywhere* in the text (regex de-anchored + `finditer`); (2) the whole stripped text as raw JSON; (3) `_extract_first_json_object` — a brace-depth scanner (string/escape-aware) that pulls the first balanced `{…}` object out of surrounding prose. Validated against the **real captured 26KB Opus 4.8 output**: parses cleanly to 14 IR rules + 17 plates + a full-color palette (sandy blonde hair, light warm skin, cool blue eyes, navy shirt, gray jeans) — Opus 4.8 authored full-color rules naturally from the notes + anchor (decision (e) honored at authoring time).
- **Accurate stub detection.** The synthetic stub envelope now carries a `_pass1_stub` marker; `run()` ORs it into `pass1_stub` so the loud-fail guard fires on the non-empty-but-unparseable case too — the exact path that slipped past commit 2b's response-field-only check on the live re-bake.
- **5 new tests:** prose-wrapped fence extraction; no-fence balanced-brace fallback; bare-fence + raw-JSON regression; and the unparseable-nonempty → `pass1_stub=True` flag. 172 green (168 + 4 parser/stub additions across 2b→2c; net +4 since the 168 baseline included 2b's 2).

**Why:** This is the second-order consequence of the Opus 4.8 bump (commit 1) — a more conversational model breaks a parser that assumed terse structured output. The capture-the-raw-output discipline (rather than guessing) pinpointed it in one shot, and the fix is model-agnostic robustness that will hold as models get chattier. With this, live Bible authoring under 4.8 works end-to-end; the clean re-bake follows.

## 2026-05-29 — Commit 2b: Opus 4.8 Pass-1 timeout fix + loud stub-fallback (surfaced by the first live re-bake)

**What changed:** The first live re-bake under Opus 4.8 (non-destructive scratch copy of sean-anchor) **silently stubbed** — it ran for exactly 900s, hit Cy's Pass-1 timeout, returned empty text, and the parser fell back to a STUB FALLBACK envelope (0 plates, placeholder rules) while `author_bible.py` still exited 0. This is precisely the "a successful exit code can lie about what actually happened" failure mode the 2026-05-28 test report named. Two fixes, plus the mechanism validation that came out of debugging it.

- **Root cause: Opus 4.8 is slower on the large Pass-1 emission.** Opus 4.7 authored the ~50KB envelope in ~500s; 4.8 spends more on extended thinking for the same structured emission and exceeded the 900s ceiling. A direct small-prompt call to `claude-opus-4-8` succeeds fast (slug valid, SDK path works) — it's specifically the long envelope that ran over. **Fix:** raised Cy's Pass-1 timeout 900s → 1800s (`character_designer.py`).
- **Loud stub-fallback (the must-fix lesson).** `CharacterDesignerNode.run` now computes `pass1_stub` (true when the Opus response is stub-flagged, non-zero exit, or empty text) and surfaces `pass1_stub=True|False` in `AgentResult.notes`. `author_bible.py` checks for it and **exits non-zero with a clear diagnostic** instead of silently shipping a stub Bible. A stub can no longer masquerade as real authoring.
- **Mechanism validated end-to-end on real models (the payoff).** Debugging the stub, the commit-1 code path was exercised directly against live NB Pro for the worst drifter (`turnarounds/head-front.png`): `_resolve_generate_references` **stripped** the generated-plate reference and **injected** the anchor (resolved refs = `[anchor.png]`), `_build_nb_pro_prompt` produced the role-tag + anti-caption framing, and the real generation returned a plate that is **recognizably Sean** — blonde tousled hair, blue eyes, warm full-color skin, friendly cartoon face — versus the old monochrome romance-hero. The commit-2 similarity gate quantifies it: recovered plate **0.564** (passes) vs old drift **0.468** (below the 0.5 flag → correctly flagged). Evidence in `runs/2026-05-29-cy-sean-anchor-rebake/`.
- **2 new tests** (`tests/test_character_designer.py`): a stubbed Pass-1 is flagged `pass1_stub=True` in notes; a real envelope is `pass1_stub=False`. 168 green (166 + 2).

**Why:** The brief was explicit — "stub-fallback is a loud failure now; if a re-bake stubs, fix it before proceeding." The silent stub would otherwise have produced an approvable-looking but empty Bible. Fixing the timeout makes real re-bakes succeed; making the stub loud means the next silent failure can't slip through. The debugging incidentally produced the cleanest possible proof that the Track-A mechanism works against live models.

## 2026-05-29 — Commit 2 (Track A): the Pass-2.5 pixel-similarity gate + persisted per-plate verdicts

**What changed:** Cy now scores every plate's identity similarity against the anchor with a pixel-grounded metric *before* Gemini's prose Pass-3 fires, and persists a per-plate verdict trail to disk. This closes the load-bearing blind spot the post-mortem named (§2.3): Gemini grounds its verdict against the IR.* rule *descriptions* (prose), so a drifted plate that satisfies the named markers passes — the prose pass is structurally blind to "looks like a different character who also has those markers." A numeric pixel score sitting next to the prose verdict makes that drift visible. 166 tests green (160 + 6 new).

- **New `pipeline/agents/similarity_gate.py`.** `compute_similarity(plate, reference) → SimilarityResult(score, method, reference)` walks a method ladder: **DINOv2** cosine (best for identity) → **CLIP** cosine → **pure-PIL perceptual** (color-histogram cosine blended 0.6/0.4 with a grayscale structural correlation). DINOv2/CLIP are tried only if `torch`+`transformers`/`open_clip` import; the PIL tier is always available, so the gate adds **zero new hard dependencies** and CI stays green. `pip install torch transformers` upgrades the gate to DINOv2 with no code change — the ladder picks it up. The PIL metric is color-weighted because palette is the strongest, most angle-robust identity signal — exactly the axis the documented drift collapsed (full-color cartoon → monochrome graphite; tiny octopus → chibi humanoid).
- **Pass-2.5 wired into `character_designer._run_plate`.** After Pass 2 generates (and after each regen), `_score_plate_identity` computes similarity vs `anchor.png` and records `similarity_score` / `similarity_method` / `similarity_reference` in the plate status, flagging `similarity_flag: below_threshold` under 0.5. **It records, it does not hard-block** this commit: the coarse PIL metric is angle-sensitive (a faithful back-of-head vs a front anchor scores low for legitimate reasons), so hard-reject-before-Pass-3 would false-reject correct non-front views. The gate is wired so promoting to hard-reject is a threshold/config change once the angle-robust DINOv2 tier is active. Scoring never raises — a corrupt plate records `similarity_error` and the bake continues.
- **Per-plate verdict trail persisted.** `_persist_plate_verdicts` writes `runs/{run_id}/plate_verdicts.jsonl` — one JSONL line per plate carrying target_path + the full status (similarity score/method, Gemini verdict/confidence/cited rules, attempt count, cache key). The 2026-05-28 run left no durable per-plate signal; this fixes it. A drift Gemini passed is now reconstructable from disk after the fact.
- **6 new tests:** 4 in `tests/test_similarity_gate.py` (identical→~1; full-color vs grayscale scores strictly lower; different palette scores <0.6; method label is the PIL fallback on a deps-free machine) + 2 in `tests/test_character_designer.py` (generate plate records a float similarity_score; plate_verdicts.jsonl persisted with score + Gemini verdict). Added a `_real_png` test helper — the 1x1 `_tiny_png` placeholder is a degenerate stream PIL can't decode, which the gate correctly treats as a scoring error.

**Why:** The post-mortem's organizing lesson — "a passing critic verdict can lie about what the plate looks like, when the critic checks words instead of pixels" — needs a pixel check to land. This adds it cheaply and makes the bake-off (Track B, if it runs) and every future re-bake quantitatively scorable instead of eyeballed. Honest about the metric's current ceiling: it flags severe drift now, and the architecture is ready for the embedding upgrade that makes it a hard gate.

## 2026-05-29 — Commit 1 (Track A): the fidelity mechanism — prompt re-weighting + unconditional anchor injection + no-chaining + Opus 4.8 bump

**What changed:** The structural fix for the visual-fidelity gap, implemented as the runner becoming the source of truth for what NB Pro actually sees — not a faithful pass-through of whatever Opus emits. Code + contract changes only; the live re-bake that validates them is the next step (gated on Sean). 160 tests green (157 baseline + 3 new).

- **Unconditional anchor injection + no-chaining (`pipeline/agents/character_designer.py`).** Two new helpers — `_classify_reference` (resolves a plate reference and tags it `anchor | source_ref | generated | external | missing`) and `_resolve_generate_references` (builds the reference list the runner actually feeds). Policy: `anchor.png` is injected first on **every** `generate` plate regardless of what Opus emitted; source-refs/ angle targets are kept; references to other generated plates (anything under `turnarounds/ expressions/ props/ motion_plates/ costumes/`) are **stripped**. Fixes the `head-back`-had-no-anchor class of bug and the reference-chaining that compounded drift (post-mortem §3d — head-3quarter chained off the drifted head-front, expressions off drifted neutral).
- **Prompt re-weighting toward references, not description (`character_designer.py` + Cy addendum).** New `_build_nb_pro_prompt` wraps each plate's *short intent* in fixed reference-role-tag framing ("Image 1 is the identity anchor — match the face, hair, palette, skin tone, proportions exactly. Keep the full color.") plus an anti-caption guardrail ("Do not add any text, labels, captions…"). The verbose verbal character-descriptions that drove prompt-dominance are gone; the runner owns the framing so a too-wordy Opus prompt can't reintroduce the drift. The anti-caption line directly kills the `props/stylus.png` failure mode where meta-prose rendered as handwritten captions (§3b). Validated by Phase 0: terse + anchor recovered identity decisively.
- **Cy addendum rewrite (`pipeline/agents/prompts/cy-character-designer-context.md`).** The "prompt contract" and "reference contract" are now explicit: `prompt` is a ≤30-word plate intent (angle/expression/pose), never a character re-description, never pipeline-meta/rule-IDs. The Pass-2 description and the schema example were rewritten — the example plate's `reference_images` changed from `["anchor.png", "turnarounds/head-front.png"]` (the chaining anti-pattern it used to model) to `["anchor.png", "source-refs/turnaround-1.png"]`, and the prompt from a "cite the IR rules inline" placeholder to a terse `"neutral expression, front view, mouth closed"`.
- **Opus 4.8 bump for the authoring tier (`pipeline/agents/sdk_runners.py`).** New `OPUS_AUTHORING_MODEL = "claude-opus-4-8"`; `invoke_opus_text` (Maya's primary/resolution passes + Cy's Pass 1) routes there. Kept as a **separate constant** from `OPUS_MODEL` (Em's vision-escalation seat, still 4.7) so the bump reverts in isolation if an eval regresses. 4.8 helps *author* the fix; it is not itself the fix.
- **Three new tests** (`tests/test_character_designer.py`): anchor injected even when Opus omits it; generated-plate references stripped (no chaining) while source-refs survive; the forwarded prompt carries the role-tag framing + anti-caption guardrail.
- **Docs:** CLAUDE.md skills-map rows for Maya + Cy updated (4.7→4.8; Cy row documents the new plate-generation contract). Em's row unchanged (escalation still 4.7).

**Why:** Phase 0 proved root cause (b) prompt-dominance was the lever. This commit removes the three mechanisms that let it operate — the runner no longer forwards verbose descriptions, no longer chains off drifted plates, and always grounds generation in the anchor. The runner-as-source-of-truth design means the fix holds even if a future Opus emission regresses to wordy prompts or self-chaining. The bump is folded in per Sean's locked decision but firewalled behind its own constant for clean revert.

## 2026-05-29 — Phase 0: the disambiguating fidelity experiment (decisive — prompt-dominance, not a model ceiling)

**What changed:** Ran the §6 disambiguating experiment from the visual-fidelity post-mortem *before* touching any code — the cheap, near-free test that separates root cause (b) prompt-dominance from (c) a hard NB Pro multi-reference ceiling. Re-generated one drifted plate (`turnarounds/head-front.png`) against **anchor.png only** with a **terse, role-free prompt** ("Redraw this exact character — same face, same hair, same friendly cartoon style, front-facing head-and-shoulders view. Keep the full color.") through the unmodified skill script at `gemini-3-pro-image-preview`.

- **Result: fidelity jumped, decisively.** The output is recognizably the *same character* as the anchor — blonde tousled hair, navy tee, blue eyes, warm full-color skin, friendly rounded cartoon face — not the monochrome aquiline romance-hero the verbose-prompt plate produced. Evidence preserved at `docs/anima-test-runs/2026-05-29-phase0-fidelity-experiment/` (`anchor-only-terse-prompt-result.png` vs `drifted-head-front-BEFORE.png`).
- **This settles the b-vs-c question: (b) prompt-dominance was the lever.** NB Pro recovers identity when the prose stops re-describing the character and simply tells the model to copy the anchor. The documented multi-ref regression (c) is real but is not the binding constraint at single-anchor front view — it was being *triggered by* our own verbose character-describing prompts.
- **Decision (e) full-color confirmed natural.** The model produced the anchor's real palette unprompted; the monochrome drift was authored into the rules, not imposed by the renderer.
- **Track B reframed.** The bake-off drops from critical-path to a de-risking option; flagged for Sean at the commit-1 checkpoint rather than unilaterally descoped (Sean locked "run in parallel"). Appendix added to `docs/2026-05-29-cy-visual-fidelity-post-mortem.md`.

**Why:** The post-mortem §6 named this experiment as the thing to run first because it "settles b-vs-c" and is "nearly free." It did, and it does — Track A is now confirmed load-bearing, which means the high-value work is the prompt + runner fix (commit 1), not the expensive model migration. Recording the verdict before code so the fix sequence is grounded in evidence, not the obvious "feed it the anchor" instinct. 157 tests unaffected (no code touched this step).

## 2026-05-29 — Visual-fidelity post-mortem + fix implementation prompt + anima rename plan (analysis session, no code)

**What changed:** A Cowork analysis + brainstorm session — no code shipped — produced three planning artifacts and confirmed the 157-test baseline holds. The trigger: Sean's visual inspection of the two locked Bibles caught what the 2026-05-28 test report didn't address — the emitted plates pass Gemini's Pass-3 verification but read as a *different character* than the source-ref anchor. Poses are excellent; identity drifts. This session diagnosed where and produced the fix plan.

- **`docs/2026-05-29-cy-visual-fidelity-post-mortem.md`** — the diagnostic. Five sections: what worked (runner robustness, two locked Bibles, register-vocabulary validation, 157 green), what didn't (the plate-by-plate drift table for both Bibles), why Gemini missed it, the root-cause trace, and the fix plan. **The drift is severe and systematic across both registers.** sean-anchor's generated head/expression plates render a generic idealized "romance-hero" face, not the friendlier cartoon Sean; claude-mascot's generated plates render a generic chibi humanoid instead of the anchor's tiny octopus-critter (lost the snout, the multi-leg silhouette, the low-res blockiness, and added arms). Every drifted generated plate PASSED Pass-3.

- **The load-bearing finding — Gemini verifies prose, not pixels.** Pass-3 grounds verdicts against the IR.* rule *descriptions* Cy wrote, not against the source-ref *pixels*. A drifted plate that nominally satisfies "jaw angular at the mandibular corner" and "eyes one eye-width apart" passes, because the wrong face also has those markers. Prose rules are a lossy compression of identity — they capture named markers but are structurally blind to "looks like a different person who also has those markers." Per-plate Gemini verdicts are also not persisted to disk, so there's no audit trail. This echoes the test report's "a successful exit code can lie" one layer up: a passing critic verdict can lie about what the plate looks like, when the critic checks words instead of pixels.

- **Root-cause trace (code-read, not speculation).** References are NOT dropped: `nb_pro_runner.py:_build_skill_cmd` passes `--reference`, the skill script (`generate_image.py:101`) loads each as `types.Part.from_bytes(...)`, cache keys include reference content hashes. The mechanism is (b) **prompt-dominance** — Cy's verbose verbal character-descriptions let NB Pro synthesize a character from text and underweight the reference pixels (proven by `props/stylus.png`, which rendered the prompt's meta-prose as literal handwritten captions on the plate); plus (c) **NB Pro's own multi-ref regression** — externally documented on the Google AI dev forum (Feb–Mar 2026): "the model appears to downsample reference images so aggressively that it can't see or replicate fine details, resulting in generic or inaccurate outputs," with a sibling thread titled "Nano banana pro ignoring prompt and reference images"; plus (d) **reference-chaining** — sean's generated plates reference other generated plates (head-3quarter ← drifted head-front; expressions ← drifted neutral; head-back references no anchor at all), compounding drift, and the runner forwards exactly what Opus emits without injecting the anchor; plus (e) **register mis-spec** — the `pencil-test-colored` rules describe monochrome graphite / "no skin tone" while the anchor is full-color, so even a faithful generation diverges.

- **Three director decisions captured via AskUserQuestion (locked):** (1) **full-color is canonical Sean** — the IR rules are mis-specified toward monochrome and must be rewritten to carry the real palette; (2) **run the model bake-off in parallel** with the cheap fixes (not after), because the external evidence says NB Pro multi-ref may cap prompt-only fixes; (3) **adopt Opus 4.8 now** (released 2026-05-28, same price as 4.7, ~4× less likely to let flaws pass) for Cy + Maya, folded into the first fidelity commit.

- **`docs/2026-05-29-cy-visual-fidelity-fix-implementation-prompt.md`** — paste-ready continuation prompt for the next Claude Code (code) session. Phase 0 disambiguating experiment (anchor-only + terse prompt to separate prompt-dominance from model-limit), then Track A (prompt re-weighting with reference role-tags + unconditional anchor injection + no-chaining + Opus 4.8) and Track B (FLUX.2 / GPT-Image-2 / FLUX+LoRA bake-off scored against a new Pass-2.5 pixel-similarity gate) running concurrently, then the full-color rule rewrite once the winning model is known.

- **`docs/2026-05-29-anima-rename-plan.md`** — scoped runbook for `sw-portfolio-animation-pipeline → anima`, deferred per v2 change-map §5. Audit found the blast radius is small: exactly one load-bearing hardcoded absolute path in production code (`pipeline/generate_inbetweens.py:23`), no `pyproject.toml`/`setup.py` to update, no absolute paths in `.env`, and **zero live `code-brain/` dependencies** on the folder name (no agents-sdk schedule reads it). The `.venv` must be rebuilt (shebangs hardcode the old path). GitHub remote is already `sw-portfolio-2D-animation`, so the local rename is decoupled from the repo rename. Three workstreams (MacBook Pro / GitHub / Mac Mini) with verification commands. **Timing: ship after the fidelity fix, not before.**

- **Regression check — Maya + Em both GREEN.** 157 tests pass in a clean offline rebuild. Maya's three-call ceiling (`planner.py:146`) is an agent-side counter independent of the SDK `max_turns=10` lift — no regression. Em still rejects any uncited fail/borderline verdict (`vision_critic.py:113–117`) — the defang didn't soften the blocking contract. The closing-the-loop case 7 stays xfailed by design; flagged as the natural follow-up after the fidelity fix, not scoped here.

**Why:** The 2026-05-28 session proved the pipeline *ships*; this session proved it doesn't yet ship the *right character*. The engine truth requires the character be "recognizably itself in its intended medium" — right now it's recognizably *a* character in a beautiful medium, just not Sean's. The diagnosis matters more than the obvious "feed it the anchor" instinct because it found the real cause is layered (prompt-dominance + a documented model regression + reference-chaining + a register contract bug) and that the verification gate was masking all of it by checking prose instead of pixels. The "Gemini passes drift because rules are prose, not pixels" finding generalizes to any critic that grounds against descriptions rather than source artifacts — it's logged to PORTFOLIO-GOLD.md. Studio-manual voice maintained across all three artifacts.

## 2026-05-28 — Commit 2 final: both real Bibles authored end-to-end — defang verified, schema validated across two registers, three SDK + runner fixes surfaced and shipped along the way

**What changed:** Cy's two real Bible authoring ceremonies ran against live Opus 4.7 + NB Pro (gemini-3-pro-image-preview) + Gemini 3.1 Pro (via agy). What the previous Commit 2 entry called "scaffolded with real source material ready for Cy's authoring session" is now "two locked Bibles on disk with 33 real plates, 33 IR.* rules total across the two registers, and the structural validation that the Task 1.4.5 defang shipped at sufficient depth." Three SDK + runner fixes surfaced during the live runs and shipped in the same commits as the Bibles they unblocked — none of them had been catchable on the stub-only path because they all sat on code branches the stub fallback bypassed. The .venv picks up `google-genai` (2.7.0) + `fal-client` (1.0.0) per CLAUDE.md's documented dependencies (only Pillow was present from a prior session). Per-Bible authoring results:

- **Task 1.10 — sean-anchor Bible (commit `7e89053`)**. Style register: `pencil-test-colored` (the control case). 24 plates emitted: 16 ingested from source-refs (4 body turnarounds + 5 head turnarounds + 9 head-turn frames + 1 walk-cycle source — extra head-profile-left was authored alongside the right-side reference), 8 generated via NB Pro (4 expressions: neutral / focused / surprised / contemplative + props/stylus.png + 3 head turnaround views: front / 3-quarter / back). Generated-plate file sizes 62KB–785KB confirm real NB Pro output (not the 69-byte placeholder stub-fallback artifact). Pass 3 Gemini verification ran across all 24 plates; 1 plate (head-turn-09) flagged for human-gate after 3 rejection attempts — surfaces in plate_results, Sean reviews before Phase 6 motion work consumes it. Wall time: ~5 minutes for Pass 1 Opus (~500s on a 55KB prompt → 42KB JSON envelope), ~3 min for the 8 NB Pro generations, ~5 min for the 24 Gemini verifications including regen attempts on the human-gated plate. Live spend: ~$2–3 in NB Pro per the Image-Model-DR §2 routing ($0.15/plate × 8 generates × ~2 average attempts on the human-gated one); Opus + Gemini subscription-absorbed. The Bible's IR.* graph: 20 rules at v1.2 schema across 8 categories — costume (2), face (3), hair (2), motion (2), palette (2), prop (2), proportion (3), style (4). Locked via `pipeline bible approve` at session end. Cy's confidence-notes file (3.6KB) flags four rules for explicit Sean review before production runtime use: eyebrow-shape-relaxed-arc, hair-silhouette-medium-short, shoulder-width measurement, palette hex tolerances. The risk-bible (5.9KB) names uncovered axes in pencil-test-register vocabulary correctly: no costume variants, no motion vocabulary beyond walk + head-turn, no expressions beyond the authored four, back-view face extrapolated from front + profile silhouettes, no lit skin tones.

- **Task 1.11 — claude-mascot Bible (commit `7e6f19f`)**. Style register: `pixel-art-8bit` (the structural validation case). All five non-negotiable success criteria from the handoff PASS:
  - **(1) style_register field**: `pixel-art-8bit` (NOT `pencil-test-colored`). The post-defang Pass-1 Opus flow did not default-anchor to the addendum's Example A register despite the per-invocation brief sitting alongside that example.
  - **(2) IR.* rules in pixel-art vocabulary**: 13 rules at v1.2 schema. Categories: palette (4-indexed-color-vocabulary, no-anti-aliasing-between-steps, primary-orange-dominant-fill), style (integer-pixel-grid-no-subpixel, dither-vertical-2px-warm-brown, no-gradient-interpolation-between-palette), proportion (head-to-body-2-to-3-chibi, body-width-1-2x-head-width, silhouette-round-topped-lozenge), face (eye-deep-brown-dot-cluster, mouth-line-deep-brown-single-stroke, expression-vocabulary-three-only), anatomy (fingertip-and-crown-cream-highlight). Every rule reads as pixel-art register vocabulary at the description and ID level.
  - **(3) grep for pencil-test markers**: `grep -iE "cross-hatching|graphite|cream paper|construction lines|pencil-test"` across all four Bible artifacts returned ZERO hits. The defang held against the live authoring run.
  - **(4) risk-bible.md in pixel-art terms**: "Four-step indexed palette is brittle by design — the brittleness is the aesthetic." Lit variants escalate to a separate Bible; smooth-edge / anti-aliased renders are a different register entirely; integer-pixel-grid is structural to identity. Negative space (no motion plates, three expressions only, single outfit) phrased in register-appropriate vocabulary.
  - **(5) Pass-3 Gemini verdicts**: Every plate's cites_identity_rules grounds in 5–9 named rules from the pixel-art-8bit vocabulary. No plate cites a generic style-register concern.

  8 plates emitted: 2 ingested from anchor (turnarounds/body-front + expressions/neutral, since the anchor's pose IS the neutral front), 6 generated via NB Pro (3 turnaround views + head-front + 2 additional expressions). Plate file sizes 193KB–2.4MB confirm real NB Pro output. 1 plate (likely body-back, the extrapolated angle Cy hedged in risk-bible) flagged for human-gate after 3 Gemini rejection attempts. Wall time: ~5 min Pass 1 Opus, ~2 min Pass 2 NB Pro, ~3 min Pass 3 Gemini including regens. Live spend: ~$1–2 in NB Pro ($0.15/plate × 6 generates × ~1.5 average attempts). Locked via `pipeline bible approve` at session end.

- **SDK / runner fix #1 — claude-agent-sdk `max_turns` raised 1 → 10 (commit `7e89053`)**. The complex Pass-1 envelope (~50KB JSON: character.yaml + 15–20 IR.* rules + risk-bible + confidence-notes + plate plan) silently tripped "Reached maximum number of turns (1)" before any AssistantMessage text streamed through `_drain_csdk_query`. The empty-text path landed Cy in the stub fallback while ostensibly succeeding (exit code 0, real-looking pipeline artifacts on disk). Smoke test against the same call with `max_turns=10` succeeded in 506s with a 53KB envelope. The pre-existing tests in `tests/test_sdk_runners.py` did not catch this because they monkey-patch `_sdk_available` to False and exercise only the stub-fallback envelope shape — the real-model branch had never been exercised in CI for complex outputs. `max_turns=10` is generous; no tool grants are possible (the `allowed_tools=[]` + `disallowed_tools=[]` lists stay empty), and the SDK has room for whatever internal turn-accounting it does on extended thinking + structured output.

- **SDK / runner fix #2 — nb_pro_runner respects .env file (commit `7e89053`)**. `invoke_nb_pro`'s GEMINI_API_KEY gate now honors both the live process env AND the project `.env` file via a new `_has_gemini_api_key()` helper. The skill script behind the runner reads `--env-file` directly, so a developer with `GEMINI_API_KEY` in `.env` but not exported into the shell silently fell into stub-fallback (69-byte placeholder PNGs at every generate plate) while the skill script would have generated real images. Caught by the second sean-anchor authoring attempt — all 5 generate plates landed as identical 69-byte placeholders, the .cache/nb_pro/ entries were placeholder hashes, and Gemini Pass-3 verification ran against PNG bytes that contained no character at all. Test fixture `_isolate_env_file` (autouse in `tests/test_nb_pro_runner.py`) repoints `_ENV_FILE` at a sentinel non-existent path so the 7 existing tests that `monkeypatch.delenv("GEMINI_API_KEY")` continue to exercise the stub-fallback path correctly.

- **SDK / runner fix #3 — character_designer reference-image path resolution (commit `7e89053`)**. Cy's Pass-1 addendum example specifies character-dir-relative paths (`"anchor.png"`) but the live Opus emission was project-root-relative (`"characters/sean-anchor/anchor.png"`). The previous `_run_plate` flow prepended `character_dir` unconditionally, producing the duplicated path `characters/sean-anchor/characters/sean-anchor/anchor.png` and crashing on FileNotFoundError mid-Pass-2 on the third sean-anchor authoring attempt. The defensive fix tries `character_dir / ref` first, falls back to `_PROJECT_ROOT / ref` if that doesn't exist — same pattern the ingest-path resolver uses earlier in the same function. The fix also adds `timeout_s=900` to the `invoke_opus_text` call (default 120s would have timed out at the previous Cy session's ~500s wall time even if max_turns hadn't been the proximate trigger).

- **NB Pro model slug verified at first real call (commit `529cf17`)**. The placeholder default `"nano-banana-pro"` in nb_pro_runner.py was a guess from the Cy brainstorm prose vocabulary; the shipped google-genai API slug per docs/Image-Model-DR-2026/prompt-3-perplexity.md:447 is `gemini-3-pro-image-preview`. The pre-flight commit updated the default before the first paid call so all 14 real NB Pro generations across the two Bibles ran against the correct model. The slug worked first try — no fallback to gemini-3.1-pro-image-preview was needed per Sean's pre-flight directive.

- **The `_build_skill_cmd` subprocess invocation uses `sys.executable`, not "python3" (commit `529cf17`)**. The PATH-based shape silently failed against system Python 3.14 where google-genai isn't installed; the fix pins the subprocess to `.venv/bin/python3.13` unconditionally. Without this, the skill script subprocess would import-fail (`ModuleNotFoundError: No module named 'google'`) even with google-genai installed in .venv, because the subprocess inherited PATH from the caller and resolved `python3` against the system interpreter.

- **Cy's scratch scripts as process-artifact evidence**. Cy emitted 27 Python diagnostic scripts during the sean-anchor Pass 1 (find_blue_back.py, measure_proportions.py, count_torso_lines.py, sample_tee_flats.py, etc.) and 3 during the claude-mascot Pass 1 (analyze_eye.py, analyze_mouth.py, grid_check.py). These are Cy verifying rule measurements against source-refs/anchor pixel data before authoring the IR.* descriptions — the eye-dot-cluster rule cites "typically one to four adjacent pixels in clusters" because Cy's analyze_eye.py measured the actual cluster size against anchor.png. Moved to `runs/2026-05-28-cy-{sean,claude-mascot}-bake/cy-scratchpad/` as process-artifact evidence per brainstorm ROT1 (bible-walkthrough museum content). Bidirectional provenance: the IR rules cite `#region:` source-ref pointers; the scratch scripts cite the rules they were measuring against. The handoff's expectation that "Pass-3 Gemini verdict JSONs are portfolio content per the museum-capture layer" is unfulfilled by the current contract (verdicts are returned in AgentResult.outputs but not persisted to disk) — a follow-up commit can wire the verdicts into a per-run `plate_verdicts.json` so the museum capture has a stable artifact to render against.

**Verification report:** Test suite holds at the baseline: `tests/` 157 passed (no behavioral changes to stub-fallback paths from the three runner fixes; the new `_isolate_env_file` autouse fixture preserves intent of the 7 existing tests). `evals/` 10 passed + 2 xfailed + 1 xpassed (planner suite + character-designer suite unchanged). The closing-the-loop test (case 7 — `closing-the-loop-em-cites-cy-rules`) stays xfailed. That case flips green in a subsequent commit when Em's prompt loads the merged CriteriaBundle including both `IR.sean.*` and `IR.claude-mascot.*` rules at run start — at that point Em can cite an `IR.claude-mascot.style.integer-pixel-grid-no-subpixel` violation on a smooth-edged Phase 5 mascot frame as concretely as it cites `IR.sean.prop.stylus-right-hand-always` on a stylus-in-left-hand Phase 5 Sean frame. The diff IS the museum content documenting the moment Bible authoring became contract-grounded across registers.

**Why:** The structural-fix-at-the-source thesis from cross-source synthesis §5 (validators cannot recover taste that was absent at generation time) demanded Bible authoring against actual diverse material, not against the convenient pencil-test single-case the v1 sketch would have biased toward. The two real Bibles together pressure-test the architecture in a way the schema-only commit 2 could not. Sean-anchor proves the contract layer works end-to-end against real material (Sean's hand-drawn turnaround, head-turn, walk-cycle, anchor) — but is a control case because Sean IS pencil-test-colored and any decent emission would have looked correct. Claude-mascot is the structural test: a categorically different register with closed indexed palette + integer-pixel-grid + chibi proportion, authored against a fundamentally different source-ref set. If Cy's Pass-1 emission had carried a single pencil-test marker into the mascot's Bible, the defang would have failed and the entire portfolio thesis (anima as a 2D animation pipeline, not a pencil-test pipeline) would be unproven. All five criteria passed; the defang held. The three runner fixes that shipped along the way are themselves portfolio content — each one was caught at a specific authoring-run failure mode that no test could have caught because they sat on real-model code branches the stub fallback bypassed. They demonstrate the v2 brainstorm-v2 §2.2 architectural-diversity argument empirically: a stub-only test suite is necessary but not sufficient; the real-model branch needs real-model authoring runs to find the failures the stubs hide. The `sys.executable` subprocess pinning, the `.env` gate, and the defensive path resolution are now the "shapes that work" — future agent fleet members (Annie, Codie, Sage) will inherit these patterns from the Cy reference implementation. The Bibles + the fixes + the scratchpad scripts together are the receipts for the v2 commitment that Bible authoring is contract-grounded, not decorative. Studio-manual voice maintained throughout — the CHANGELOG entry, the commit messages, the risk-bibles, the confidence-notes, the in-tree CLI output. The 27-script sean-anchor scratchpad reads as "the working illustrator's notebook" — measurements scribbled before the rule got written down — and is portfolio-grade evidence that the IR.* descriptions are grounded in observable signal rather than interpretive prose. Sean's portfolio thesis depends on anima being a 2D animation pipeline that ships pencil-test as its first reference register without leaking pencil-test bias into the rest of the architecture; the two real Bibles + the post-defang validation make that commitment concrete.

## 2026-05-28 — Commit 2: Cy the Character Designer + two real Bibles scaffolded + style-neutrality defang + guardrail

**What changed:** Commit 2's main event ships Cy — anima's character designer — as a three-phase AgentSpec (Opus 4.7 authors → NB Pro generates → Gemini 3.1 Pro verifies), plus the Bible CLI surface, plus the manifest schema extensions that wire per-Bible criteria into the runtime, plus the Maya project-type routing that scopes Bible-authoring runs to Phase 0 + Phase 2, plus the load-bearing pencil-test-bias defang that converts anima from a pencil-test pipeline pretending to be a 2D pipeline into a 2D pipeline that ships pencil-test as its first reference register. Twelve commits across the day, six new Python modules, three new prompt files, two new templates, four new test files (45 new tests; suite grows from 122 → 157 green), one new doctrine note, two character folders scaffolded with real source material ready for Cy's authoring session, one orchestrator script. Headline structural results: (a) the AgentSpec contract for Cy mirrors Maya's three-phase shape verbatim with categorically different per-pass model assignments — proving the AgentSpec protocol generalizes across taste-call-then-generate-then-verify workflows, not just plan-then-validate-then-revise workflows; (b) the `IR.{character_id}.{category}.{handle}` namespace inside the existing `acceptance_criteria.json` graph schema makes Bible identity rules first-class criteria Em can cite at T2-critic time without new wiring; (c) the `style_register` closed vocabulary (`pencil-test-colored | pixel-art-8bit | line-art-only | watercolor | photoreal | 3d-rendered`) makes style a Bible-level top-level attribute Flo's Phase 5 routing reads, not a downstream prompt detail; (d) the defang + the guardrail together close the structural gap the prompts had — pencil-test was the implicit default in four files (anima-standing-context.md L37 Template-trap drift, cy-character-designer-context.md L135-181 "What good looks like" examples, em-vision-critic-context.md L52 Aesthetic drift, maya-planner-context.md L98-99 sample criterion) plus character_designer.py:380's stub-fallback envelope. Per-task highlights:

- **Task 1.1 (commit 643d8bc) — criteria.py extended with IR.* namespace, character_id, plate-region pointers.** v1.2 schema lands; v1.1 + v1.0 continue to load unchanged. Closed `VALID_IR_CATEGORIES = {anatomy, hair, face, proportion, palette, costume, prop, pose, motion, style}` mirrors the Maya v1.1 `VALID_CATEGORIES` pattern. IR.* records require `character_id` field that matches the parsed prefix. `derived_from` accepts `#region:X` plate-pointer suffix as opaque metadata for museum surfacing. Eight new tests under `tests/test_criteria_ir_namespace.py`.

- **Task 1.2 (commit dcc2cf9) — NB Pro runner wrapper with content-addressed cache + reject-aware invalidation.** `pipeline/agents/nb_pro_runner.py` shells out to the existing `.claude/skills/gemini-pencil-animation-image-gen/scripts/generate_image.py` with a typed response envelope (`NBProResponse: output_path, cache_key, cache_hit, stub_fallback, exit_code`). Cache key SHA-256s prompt + sorted ref-image content hashes + `cites_identity_rules` tuple + `reject_reason` + model — the `reject_reason` thread is what makes `cy iterate --reject ...` regenerations invalidate the cache for specific plates without re-running the whole Bible. Stub fallback writes a 1×1 transparent PNG when `GEMINI_API_KEY` is missing. Seven new tests.

- **Task 1.3 (commit 3461c67) — character.yaml + source-refs templates (studio-manual voice).** `templates/bible/character.yaml.template` carries the load-bearing identity-contract schema with anchored prose comments around every field; `templates/bible/source-refs-checklist.md` is the blank-page-tax handoff Cy reads when Sean drops material.

- **Task 1.4 (commit 4c00937) — Cy's standing-context preamble.** `pipeline/agents/prompts/cy-character-designer-context.md` mirrors Maya's role-addendum structure: persona introduction, five-artifact contract, IR.* graph contract, three-phase flow, non-negotiables, the closing-the-loop expectation, the lens Cy brings vs the lenses she doesn't, worked example. The 2d-animation-principles skill loads as an inline appendix per ENG5 (folded into TOP-3) — Cy reads animation physics before authoring motion-plate rules.

- **Task 1.5 (commit c869b0b) — Cy's three-phase AgentSpec.** `pipeline/agents/character_designer.py` registered as `@register_node("character_designer")`. Pass 1 Opus authors the five-artifact JSON envelope (character.yaml + ir_entries + risk_bible_md + cy_confidence_notes_md + plate_generation_plan). Pass 2 reads the plate plan, walks each entry, ingests source-ref pixels for `source: "ingest:..."` plates or calls NB Pro for `source: "generate"` plates. Pass 3 runs Gemini against every plate via the same `run_antigravity_with_image` wrapper Em uses; verdict envelope routes to plate_results with a three-attempt ceiling per plate. Fail at attempt 3 surfaces `status: human_gate_required` in plate_results — the Bible doesn't fail because of one stubborn plate; it surfaces the stubborn one. Nine new tests including ingested-plate-still-verifies, three-attempt-ceiling-surfaces-human-gate, gemini-fail-triggers-regen-with-reject-reason, box-characters-forbidden in risk-bible.md + cy-confidence-notes.md.

- **Task 1.6 (commit 093c143) — cost estimator Phase 2 row.** `pipeline/agents/cost_estimator.py` removes phase_2 from `SUBSCRIPTION_ABSORBED_PHASES` and adds `_phase_2_cost(manifest)` that reads each registered character's `plate_generation_plan.json` from disk and prices generate plates at $0.15 NB Pro (Image-Model-DR §2). Ingested plates contribute $0. Median band assumes ~30% regen rate; high band assumes 3-attempt ceiling per plate. Four new tests.

- **Task 1.7 (commit 6e840d8) — pipeline bible init/show/approve/mutate/iterate CLI.** `pipeline/cli/bible.py` mirrors `pipeline/cli/plan.py` structurally; `pipeline/cli/__main__.py` wires the subparser. `show` is the rendering layer — ANSI background-color palette swatches, identity rules grouped by IR category, motion plate inventory, risk-bible callouts, Cy's confidence hedges — boxes live in the renderer, not on disk. `mutate` writes one JSONL line per call to `runs/{run_id}/bible_audit.jsonl`. `iterate` writes a narrowed `plate_generation_plan_iterate.json` with `reject_reason` threaded per plate.
