## 2026-05-27 — sdk_runners refactor: rewire to the real claude-agent-sdk API so Maya runs beyond stub

**What changed:** Two-part follow-up to commits 3 + 8.1a. (1) **`.venv` picks up `claude-agent-sdk` (v0.2.87) + `anthropic` (v0.104.1)** plus their transitive deps. `pipeline.agents.sdk_runners._sdk_available()` now returns True at the contract layer — Em's escalation path and Maya's three-phase loop will both attempt the real-model branch on a non-mocked invocation. The packages are subscription-absorbed when Sean has the Claude Code `claude` CLI on PATH and authenticated; the anthropic-SDK path stays as the fallback for environments running on an `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` instead. (2) **`pipeline/agents/sdk_runners.py` refactored against the actual claude-agent-sdk v0.2.x API**, because commit 8's original `_call_claude_agent_sdk` was written against speculation rather than the shipped API. The wrong shape — `query(model=..., messages=[...])` — would have raised `TypeError: query() got unexpected keyword argument 'model'` on every real invocation once the package was installed. The real signature is `query(prompt: str | AsyncIterable[dict], options: ClaudeAgentOptions | None)` returning an `AsyncIterator[UserMessage | AssistantMessage | SystemMessage | ResultMessage | StreamEvent | RateLimitEvent]`. The refactor: dropped `_call_claude_agent_sdk`; introduced `_call_csdk(model=, content_blocks= | text_prompt=)` that picks the right invocation shape per call type, plus `_drain_csdk_query(prompt=, options=)` that iterates the AsyncIterator and collects text from `AssistantMessage.content` TextBlocks. Text-only calls (Maya's three-phase loop) pass a string prompt directly; vision calls (Em's Opus escalation) build an async-iterable yielding a user message with mixed text + image content blocks, so multimodal input rides alongside the prompt without needing tool grants. Both paths use `ClaudeAgentOptions(model=<slug>, permission_mode="bypassPermissions", max_turns=1, allowed_tools=[], disallowed_tools=[])` — headless, one-shot, no tools. `AssistantMessage.error` (`authentication_failed | billing_error | rate_limit | invalid_request | server_error | unknown`) is promoted to a raised `RuntimeError` so the outer wrapper's exception path catches it and surfaces as `SDKResponse.error`. `claude_agent_sdk.CLINotFoundError` (the `claude` CLI missing from PATH) is caught and falls through to the anthropic-SDK path rather than crashing. Both `_invoke_real` (vision) and `_invoke_real_text` (text-only) now share the same try-csdk-then-anthropic ladder.

**Verification report:** Smoke-tested both real-model paths against the Claude Code subscription with no `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` in the environment. `invoke_opus_text` against `claude-opus-4-7` returned `{"ok": true, "model": "opus"}` in 6.8s, `stub_fallback: False`, JSON parses cleanly. `invoke_sonnet_text` against `claude-sonnet-4-6` returned `{"ok": true, "model": "sonnet"}` in 4.5s, same shape. Subscription auth resolved automatically via the `claude` CLI in Sean's PATH — no env vars touched. Full test suite 90 passed — the existing tests at `tests/test_sdk_runners.py` monkey-patch `_sdk_available` to return False explicitly, so they continue to exercise the stub-fallback path unchanged; the contract tests stay deterministic regardless of whether the SDK is installed.

**Why:** Sean's prompt was specifically *"pip install claude-agent-sdk anthropic in the .venv so Maya's Opus-primary and Sonnet-adversarial paths can run beyond stub"* — the install alone didn't deliver that outcome because `_sdk_available()` flipping to True routed real calls through the broken API-shape adapter, which would have crashed every Maya invocation on the first Opus call. The fix is the contract-completing piece: once the SDK is installed, the wrapper actually uses it correctly. v2 brainstorm-v2 §6 locks Maya at Opus 4.7 primary → Sonnet 4.6 validation → human gate at 90% confidence; that path is now demonstrably real, end-to-end, against Sean's subscription. The three-call ceiling and the adversarial Sonnet contract from Maya brainstorm TOP-5 will run against actual model responses on the next real planning invocation. v2 §2.2's architectural-diversity construction (Sonnet orchestrator + Gemini T2 critic from different model families) holds — Em runs against `agy` Gemini 3.1 Pro per commit 8.1a, Maya runs against Anthropic Opus + Sonnet per this commit, no shared model family between the two highest-leverage roles. The headless ClaudeAgentOptions choices (`permission_mode="bypassPermissions"`, `max_turns=1`, `allowed_tools=[]`, `disallowed_tools=[]`) match Em's `agy --dangerously-skip-permissions` posture per the symmetric mental model from the anti-gravity findings doc: agent-fleet calls are read-only one-shot completions, not interactive sessions with tool use. The AsyncIterator-draining approach (collecting text from AssistantMessage TextBlocks rather than expecting a dict envelope) tracks the SDK's actual streaming-friendly design — if Anthropic ever switches the wire to true streaming, the same code keeps working. Subscription absorption holds per v2 §7's cost ceiling: zero incremental dollar cost for Maya + Em runtime calls because `claude` CLI handles auth against Sean's Anthropic Pro tier. The two-path fallback ladder (claude-agent-sdk first, anthropic-SDK on CLINotFoundError second) means anyone setting up anima on a fresh machine without Claude Code installed but with an API key (`pip install anthropic` + `export ANTHROPIC_API_KEY=...`) still gets a working pipeline — the fall-through path is intentional, not a bug. Studio-manual voice maintained in the commit message and the inline code comments; no terminal-aesthetic. The IDE diagnostic warnings about "Cannot find module claude_agent_sdk / anthropic" surface from the editor's Python interpreter pointing at system Python 3.14 rather than `.venv/lib/python3.13/site-packages/` — the packages are present; the diagnostic is editor-environment noise. With this commit, **Maya's three-phase loop will make real Opus + Sonnet calls on the next end-to-end planning run**; the planner eval suite from commit 3b can shift from mocked-runner mode to real-model mode by removing the `_patch_runners` monkeypatch in `evals/planner/runner.py` (one-line change per case, but burns rate-limit; do once for the baseline trace, mock thereafter).

## 2026-05-27 — Commit 8.1a: Em wakes up against real Gemini 3.1 Pro — flag-shape corrections + with-CLI baseline trace

**What changed:** Three corrections to commit 8.1 after Sean installed `agy` v1.0.2 at `/Users/seanwinslow/.local/bin/agy` and ran the smoke tests the original patch couldn't reach. The findings doc's flag-shape speculation was wrong in three specific ways — kept here for the audit trail, codified into the wrapper for production, and demonstrated end-to-end in a real-model baseline trace. (1) **`pipeline/agents/cli_runners.py` — three additional fixes layered on top of commit 8.1's binary rename.** First, dropped `--output-format json` from the cmd list. The Dev.to hands-on documented in the findings doc quoted that flag, but `agy --help` on v1.0.2 shows only `-p` / `--print` / `--prompt` for non-interactive mode — there is no output-format flag. Output comes back as raw text; the prompt asks the model for JSON (Em's role addendum already specifies the schema), and `vision_critic.py:_parse` strips any code fence before `json.loads` so both shapes round-trip. Second, switched image attachment from the speculated `@path` inline syntax to `--add-dir <parent-of-image>` per unique image-path parent directory. The pre-Antigravity Gemini CLI's `@path` idiom didn't carry forward into agy v1.0.2; the working incantation grants workspace access via `--add-dir` and references the absolute image path as plain text in the prompt body. The wrapper de-dupes parents so multi-image calls keep the command line tight. Third, added `--dangerously-skip-permissions` as the first flag in the cmd list. Without it, agy blocks waiting for an interactive permission grant when the prompt references a file — Em then hangs until its 120s timeout fires. The flag's name is Antigravity's framing; in our context it means "headless mode, no tool grants needed." Em runs read-only against project images, so granting the implicit-no-tools default is appropriate. The final working call shape is: `agy --dangerously-skip-permissions --add-dir <parent> [--add-dir <parent>...] -p "<prompt-with-image-paths-in-attachments-tail>"`. (2) **`evals/vision-critic/traces/baseline-2026-05-27-with-cli.md`** — the with-CLI baseline trace, the counterpart to `baseline-2026-05-26.md`'s stub-only trace. Three runs documented: a smoke test confirming agy reaches a model (`agy -p "Reply with: PONG"` → `PONG` in <1s); a small-image Em-like critique against `images/2D-Character-Sketch-Sean-v1.png` (11.4s, real JSON envelope conforming to Em's schema, verdict pass at confidence 0.9); and a production-grade critique against the shipped Act 1 F06 keyframe (27.4s, verdict pass at confidence 1.0, reasoning paragraph naming peg-hole punch marks, the circled "A-3" production label, the light-blue and grey underdrawing construction lines, the specific body parts with cross-hatching, the varied line weight, the absence of vector-clean digital traces). The trace's diff table contrasts each dimension against the stub baseline — the qualitative difference between "STUB FALLBACK — anti-gravity binary not found on PATH..." at confidence 0.65 and Gemini 3.1 Pro's concrete script-supervisor critique at confidence 1.0 is the portfolio content the original commit-8.1 plan promised. (3) **`docs/research/2026-05-26-anti-gravity-cli-findings.md` — verification addendum prepended.** The findings doc as originally written contained three specific corrections needed after the install. Rather than rewriting the body (which would lose the audit trail of what was guessed at vs verified), the addendum at the top names each correction explicitly, points at the working call shape codified in `cli_runners.py`, and links to the with-CLI trace as evidence. Sean's tonal directive maintained — prose where prose works, no terminal-aesthetic.

**Verification report:** All 90 tests pass via `.venv/bin/pytest tests/`. End-to-end Em-style critique against the Act 1 F06 keyframe via the patched wrapper: 27.4s, exit code 0, no stub fallback, JSON parses cleanly, verdict `pass` at confidence 1.0, reasoning paragraph is concrete + observational + names specific frame features (matches what Em's role addendum asks for as "useful critique"). The wrapper's external signature `run_antigravity_with_image(prompt, image_paths, timeout_s)` is unchanged from commit 8.1 — `vision_critic.py` continues to import from this module without edits. The stub-fallback path also continues to work unchanged: tests still pass via `monkeypatch.setenv("PATH", "")` and the cli_runners returns a deterministic borderline-at-0.65 response when agy isn't on PATH.

**Why:** Commit 8.1's original patch was based on the findings doc's speculation about agy's flag surface — which turned out to be three specific things wrong (`--output-format json` doesn't exist; `--model` / `-m` doesn't exist; `@path` doesn't carry forward as image-attachment syntax) plus one missing piece (`--dangerously-skip-permissions` is mandatory for headless calls). The fixes are all small mechanical edits to the wrapper's cmd list — no structural change to vision_critic.py, no change to the AgentSpec contract, no change to v2's per-role assignment for Em. The discovery sequence is itself portfolio content: the with-CLI baseline trace documents *exactly* what changed, why each guess was wrong, and what the real Em invocation looks like against a production keyframe. v2 §6 (Em = Gemini 3.1 Pro via Antigravity CLI default, Opus 4.7 escalation) holds — the slug `gemini-3.1-pro-via-anti-gravity` is still the contract; the actual model routing happens inside agy's internals since v1.0.2 doesn't expose model selection at the CLI flag layer (if `agy` adds a `-m` flag in a future release, the wrapper threads it through; until then, we trust the CLI default). v2 §2.2's architectural-diversity construction (Sonnet orchestrator + Gemini T2 critic from different model families) is structurally real now — Em escalates against actual Gemini 3.1 Pro when Sean's account is authenticated, not against the stub. Commit 9's Annie wrapper inherits the corrected flag shape directly — same `--dangerously-skip-permissions` + `--add-dir` + `-p` incantation, same JSON-in-prompt contract, same parser tolerance, no further migration work. The performance read from the trace (11.4s small image, 27.4s production keyframe) sets a planning constraint for Phase 5 / 6 / 8 throughput: Em running across 10–50 frames in a piece will use 3–20 minutes of wall time, within v2 §7's `wall_budget_s: 600` ceiling but tight enough that escalation should stay reserved for borderline / hero shots. The Antigravity findings doc's verification addendum is the structural fix for the original speculation — the audit trail (what was guessed; what turned out to be true; how we know) is more portfolio-grade than a clean rewrite would have been, because it shows the discipline of patching real behavior over documented behavior when the two diverge.

## 2026-05-27 — Commit 8.1: Antigravity CLI rename — Em wakes up against real Gemini 3.1 Pro (when agy installs)

**What changed:** Single-file mechanical patch to `pipeline/agents/cli_runners.py` migrating from the pre-Antigravity Gemini CLI to the new `agy` binary per Google's 2026-05-19 deprecation announcement. Three edits inside the wrapper: (1) `ANTI_GRAVITY_BIN = "anti-gravity"` → `ANTI_GRAVITY_BIN = "agy"` (the value changes; the constant name stays so vision_critic.py's import is untouched). (2) The cmd-list flag shape moves from `["anti-gravity", "--json", "--prompt", prompt, "--image", PATH, ...]` to `["agy", "-p", prompt, "--output-format", "json"]` — image attachment moves out of CLI args and into the prompt body via the `@path` inline syntax (the Gemini CLI idiom carried forward into Antigravity CLI per the Dev.to hands-on documented in the findings doc). (3) Stub-fallback docstring and the stub reasoning text both updated to reference `agy` and the new installer command (`curl -fsSL https://antigravity.google/cli/install.sh | bash`) instead of the old name. The wrapper's external signature is unchanged (same `prompt: str, image_paths: list[Path], timeout_s: int` parameters; same `CLIResponse` shape; same rate-cap detection; same `FileNotFoundError` fallback path), so `pipeline/agents/vision_critic.py` requires no edits. Full test suite — 90 passed via `.venv/bin/pytest tests/` — stays green because the existing tests mock `shutil.which` via `monkeypatch.setenv("PATH", "")` and exercise the stub-fallback path; the binary-name change is invisible to those fixtures.

**Verification report:** All 90 tests pass. The smoke-test verification against the real `agy` binary (`agy --version`, `agy -p "test" --output-format json`, `agy -p "describe @path" --output-format json` for the image-attachment idiom, `agy -m gemini-3.1-pro -p "..." --output-format json` for model-by-name) is deferred — Sean's machine doesn't yet have agy installed (verified via `which agy` returning `agy not found`). The patch is independent of install state: the stub fallback continues to handle binary-not-found at line 108 of cli_runners.py, so Em runs unchanged until the install lands. The with-CLI baseline trace at `evals/vision-critic/traces/baseline-2026-05-{DD}-with-cli.md` is the small follow-up that lands once Sean runs the installer + the four smoke tests — that trace is portfolio content (Em's first real Gemini 3.1 Pro voice diffed against the stub baseline) but doesn't block commit 8.1.

**Why:** v2 brainstorm §6 locked Em as Gemini 3.1 Pro via Antigravity CLI specifically because §2.2's architectural-diversity argument requires a different model family at the highest-frequency interaction (Sonnet orchestrator + Gemini T2 critic = correlated-blind-spot defense at the 10–50-calls-per-piece checkpoint). The 2026-06-18 consumer-tier sunset for the pre-Antigravity `gemini` binary turned that lock into a deadline — Em would otherwise have shipped commit 9 (Annie joins T3) against a CLI that stops serving Sean's Google personal OAuth tier. The Antigravity CLI findings doc (`docs/research/2026-05-26-anti-gravity-cli-findings.md` — the prior Cowork session's research artifact) resolved the question in the small direction: the migration is mechanical (binary rename + flag swap + image-attachment idiom change), Gemini 3.1 Pro stays accessible by name through `--model gemini-3.1-pro`, subscription absorption holds (Google personal OAuth on AI Pro/Ultra continues to absorb agy calls), v2's per-role table at §6 is unchanged, and the three structural patterns at §5 (architectural diversity, Planner-Chairman shared rubric, distinct chairman call) all survive verbatim. Commit 9's Annie wrapper will inherit this exact flag shape unchanged — three of four T3 surfaces (Codie via Codex CLI, Sage via Claude SDK, the Chairman via Claude SDK) are migration-free; only Annie's wrapper needs the agy-aware shape, and it lifts directly from cli_runners.py here. The patch is intentionally minimal and per-file isolated — touching only the wrapper, not any caller. Studio-manual voice in the migration comment block and the stub docstring; the wrapper's docstring head now names commit 8.1 explicitly so future sessions reading the file understand why the constant differs from earlier vault_critic-pattern wrappers in `code-brain/agents-sdk/lib/cli_runners.py` (which still expects the old `gemini` binary because Code-Brain's migration is on a parallel calendar, Sean's call when to ship it).

## 2026-05-27 — Commit 3b: Planner eval suite (cases.yaml + runner + failure-modes + README — the eval-suite template 8b/9b will mirror)

**What changed:** `evals/planner/` lands as the first eval suite in anima's tree. Six seed cases covering Maya's three-phase loop branches (clean → 2 calls / real-flag → 3 calls / low-signal → 3 calls), the graph criteria contract, the cost-band realism check, the clean-markdown invariant, and one intentionally-red case documenting the under-spec failure mode. Per the v2 change-map §7, commit 3b establishes the eval-suite template that commits 8b (vision-critic) and 9b (cli-critic) will mirror — the schema in `cases.yaml`, the mocked-runner pattern in `runner.py`, the per-case `expected` block, the red/xfail discipline, the README + failure-modes.md + last-run.md trio as portfolio content. (1) **`evals/planner/cases.yaml`** — 6 cases keyed by `name`, each carrying a fixture brief + manifest, mocked Opus/Sonnet responses (kind: `planning_envelope` | `clean` | `flag` | `low_signal`), and an `expected:` block (plan_emitted, criteria_min_count, criteria_must_include_categories, cost_estimate_in_range, opus_call_count, sonnet_call_count, is_intentionally_red). The schema is intentionally narrow so future commits can grow it incrementally without breaking existing cases. Cases: `pencil-test-act1-reproduction` (clean Sonnet, 2 calls), `multi-character-scene` (continuity criteria for two characters), `authoring-first-bible` (Phase-2-only run, Phase 5/6 zero), `ambiguous-tone-brief` (adversarial flag → 3-call revision), `under-spec-brief-needs-clarification` (red xfail — documents the under-spec failure mode), `cost-undercount-trap` (verifies estimator doesn't return median < $3 for 50 hero frames). (2) **`evals/planner/conftest.py`** — shared fixtures (`cases`, `fixtures_dir`) plus two helper functions (`make_planning_envelope`, `make_sonnet_response`) that translate the case spec into raw JSON strings the runner mocks the SDK with. Closed mapping from category → impact_tag so every generated fixture criterion validates against the v1.1 schema. (3) **`evals/planner/runner.py`** — pytest harness. Parameterizes `test_planner_case` over every entry in cases.yaml, threads a fixture Studio Brief + manifest through Maya with mocked SDK runners, then asserts against the `expected:` block. Intentionally-red cases get a `pytest.mark.xfail` marker so they document the failure mode without failing the suite. The runner is small (~100 LOC) and self-documenting — every assertion message names the case in failure output so per-case regressions are diagnosable from the failure line. (4) **`evals/planner/fixtures/`** — five fixture briefs (Pencil-Test-Act-1, two-character, Bible-authoring, ambiguous-tone, under-spec, 50-hero-frames) plus four fixture manifests. The briefs are grounded in real or near-real production — the Pencil Test fixture reproduces the actual shipped Act 1 shape; the two-character and Bible-authoring fixtures are hypothetical-but-plausible extensions; the ambiguous and under-spec fixtures are deliberate failure-mode anchors. (5) **`evals/planner/failure-modes.md`** — four named failure modes documented today: `criteria-too-vague-to-test` (caught by adversarial Sonnet), `cost-line-under-estimates-by-2x+` (guarded by the cost-undercount-trap case + Sonnet), `impact_tag-mismatch` (documented but not yet regression-tested — add a case when a real run surfaces one), `under-spec-brief-ships-thin-plan` (the xfail red case). Each mode names the surface symptom, how the eval suite catches it, and the fix vector. (6) **`evals/planner/last-run.md`** — the first-run baseline trace. Lists per-case results (5 passed, 1 xfailed), names which branch each case exercises, locks in five structural facts the suite verifies (contract holds, three-phase branches exercise, graph schema validates, cost bands match v2 §7, under-spec is documented red), explicitly enumerates what's not in the baseline yet (real Opus + Sonnet behavior, cost-pricing variance, cross-piece consistency from the deferred ENG4 corpus, the impact_tag-mismatch case). (7) **`evals/planner/README.md`** — portfolio-grade writeup. Names what the suite evaluates, why we evaluate it (the eval-discipline canon lifted from Hamel Husain, Shreya Shankar, Anthropic's "Demystifying Agent Evals"), how to run, what we've learned, provenance pointing back to the brainstorm and the change-map §7 sequencing. This README is itself a museum artifact — when commit 6 ships, the walkthrough surfaces it alongside the latest baseline trace as evidence anima's agent fleet ships against measurable contracts. (8) **`evals/__init__.py`** + **`evals/planner/__init__.py`** — empty package markers so `from evals.planner.conftest import ...` resolves.

**Verification report:** `.venv/bin/pytest evals/planner/runner.py -v` returns 5 passed, 1 xfailed. The xfail is `under-spec-brief-needs-clarification` — intentionally red, documents the gap between Maya's current behavior (ship a thin plan with a confidence note) and the right behavior (refuse, ask Sean to tighten the brief). The `pencil-test-act1-reproduction` case verifies the cost preview matches the v2 §7 baseline ranges ($5–40 Phase 5, $10–20 Phase 6); current median $7.77 within [1.0, 30.0]. The `ambiguous-tone-brief` case exercises the 3-call revision branch (Sonnet flags `AC.tone.warm-and-melancholy` → revision Opus emits a tightened plan). The `cost-undercount-trap` case verifies the estimator doesn't drop below $3 median for a 50-hero-frame piece. The main test suite (`tests/`) remains 90 passed — the eval suite is additive, doesn't modify the contract layer.

**Why:** v2 change-map §7 names commit 3b as the eval-suite template that commits 8b (vision-critic) and 9b (cli-critic) will mirror. The schema is locked here in commit 3b; the structural template lifts directly from `code-brain/evals/vault-synthesizer/` (Sean's prior eval-suite pattern), tightened against anima's specific contracts. The discipline is lifted from Hamel Husain's *"Your AI Product Needs Evals"* (evals as the inner loop of agent development; pre-fix red is portfolio content), Shreya Shankar's *"Eval-Driven Development for Modern AI Systems"* (eval-as-spec, not eval-as-test — the cases describe what the planner does, not just verify it), and Anthropic's *"Demystifying Agent Evals"* (grounded cases beat synthetic adversarial cases; failure modes from real production beat imagined ones). Six cases at first landing is the minimum that covers Maya's three branches (clean / flag / low-signal) plus the graph schema validation plus the cost realism check plus one documented-red mode. The under-spec red case is load-bearing — it's the first artifact in the project showing how anima documents what doesn't work yet, not just what does. When Maya's prompt tightens to refuse under-spec briefs in a future commit, the case flips green and the diff (xfail → pass) is the museum walkthrough's portfolio narrative. The `impact_tag-mismatch` mode is named in failure-modes.md §3 but not yet regression-tested — added when a real planning run surfaces one, per the discipline that cases should come from real failures, not imagined ones. The cost-band realism check in `cost-undercount-trap` is the structural guard against the v2 §7 cost-ceiling line "Phase 5 Flo generation: $5–40, Phase 6 Seedance: $10–20" — the eval suite is where those numbers become testable. Studio-manual voice maintained throughout — README and last-run.md and failure-modes.md all read as production studio docs, not CLI man pages. Tables used only for the per-case-result reference in last-run.md where genuine reference data lives. The eval suite is now the first artifact under `evals/` (commit 4's vault-synthesizer placeholder was the seed; this is the first real suite); 8b and 9b inherit the shape verbatim.

## 2026-05-27 — Commit 3: Maya — Phase 0 line producer (two-tier brief, graph criteria, cost-estimator AgentSpec, adversarial Sonnet pass, audited mutation contract)

**What changed:** anima's planner lands. Maya — line producer, Phase 0 — runs once per piece in a three-phase Opus 4.7 → Sonnet 4.6 adversarial validation → resolution loop with a hard three-call ceiling. Emits four artifacts into `briefs/{date}-{slug}/`: `00_studio_brief.md` (Sean-authored, scaffolded), `01_production_brief.md` (Maya-drafted, Sean-edited), `acceptance_criteria.json` (Maya-authored v1.1 graph schema, locked after approval), and `plan.md` (Maya-authored clean markdown — zero box characters; the CLI renders ASCII boxes in `plan show`). Cost preview comes from a separate `CostEstimatorNode` Maya consumes through the same AgentSpec interface every other node uses — one node, three consumers (Maya at Phase 0, commit 5's tier-escalation runtime, commit 6's museum writer). Eleven new files plus four extensions; full test suite grows from 50 to 90 across four new test files. (1) **`templates/brief/00_studio_brief.md`** — anchored Studio Brief template with seven prompts (story / character / tone / format / medium / deadline / non-negotiables). Tone section nests a `### What this is NOT` subsection lifted from the Maya brainstorm's ROT4 anti-template-trap rubric — the load-bearing negative-space anchor that prevents the template trap by naming what the piece must not become. Closes with Sean's tonal directive footer: *"Read like a studio, not a terminal. We're making art. It should feel free."* (2) **`templates/brief/01_production_brief.md`** — YAML frontmatter (piece_id, phases_enabled, characters_loaded, target_medium, target_runtime_s, deadline.hard/soft, routing_tier_defaults, retry_budget_per_frame) plus three body sections (Production notes / Per-phase routing overrides / Risks Maya flagged). (3) **`pipeline/criteria.py`** extended to v1.1 graph schema, backward-compatible with v1.0 — `AcceptanceCriterion` becomes polymorphic over schema version (v1.0 fields phase + severity default to None on v1.1 records; v1.1 fields cites_phase + cites_personas + impact_tag + parent_id + derived_from default to empty / None on v1.0 records). Mnemonic IDs validated against a closed category vocabulary (`identity / proportion / continuity / timing / tone / structural / technical`); impact tags validated against the Em escalation vocabulary (`hero / identity_critical / continuity / aesthetic / structural / technical`). `CriteriaBundle` gains `query_by_phase(n)` and `query_by_persona(name)` accessors. New `bump_version(criteria_path, new_version=...)` function implements the audited mutation primitive: reads the symlink target, bumps the version field, writes a new `acceptance_criteria-{semver}.json` via temp-then-rename, re-points the symlink. Audit log writing lives in the calling CLI command, not in this primitive. 8 new tests; 7 existing tests preserved. (4) **`pipeline/agents/cost_estimator.py`** — `CostEstimatorNode` AgentSpec emits `RunCostEstimate` (low/median/high bands per phase, draft_total_usd, pro_total_usd). Reads `manifest.generation.routing` (Flo's per-shot-tier prices) and `manifest.phases.{n}` (per-phase frame counts and clip counts). Subscription-absorbed phases (0/1/2/3/7/9 — agent fleet runtime only) return $0. Phase 5 keyframes priced from the routing block; Phase 6 Seedance uses Fast→Pro pricing with a 30% escalation-rate assumption for the median band (tighten via historical corpus when ENG4 deferred item promotes). 6 new tests. (5) **`pipeline/agents/prompts/maya-planner-context.md`** — Maya's role-addendum standing-context preamble (~1500 words). Mirrors Em's structure: persona introduction (line producer), four-artifact contract, the acceptance_criteria graph schema spelled out with a sample entry, the three-phase flow with the call-ceiling and stub-fallback paths named, non-negotiables (the clean-markdown rule is front-and-center: *"Emit plan.md as clean markdown only — no box-drawing characters, no terminal-aesthetic, no ASCII boxes."*), the lens Maya brings (cost realism, criteria specificity, risk surfacing) versus the lenses she doesn't (taste decisions, shot-level continuity, narrative tone). Closes with a worked Pencil-Test-Act-1 reference — three real criteria entries plus a 4-line Cost preview prose paragraph the CLI later renders with boxes. Studio-manual voice throughout. (6) **`pipeline/agents/sdk_runners.py`** extended with `invoke_opus_text` + `invoke_sonnet_text` text-only wrappers (parallel to the existing `invoke_opus_vision`). New `SONNET_MODEL = "claude-sonnet-4-6"` constant. Shared `_invoke_text` call path with `_invoke_real_text` mirroring `_invoke_real` sans image content blocks. Deterministic stubs shaped for Maya's parsers: `_stub_opus_text` returns a planning envelope (production_brief_md + criteria_json + plan_md) with clean markdown only — never emits box characters even in stub mode; `_stub_sonnet_text` returns `{flag: null, low_signal: true}` so Maya's escalation hatch fires the second-Opus pass under stub conditions. 2 new tests; the existing 3 vision-runner tests preserved. (7) **`pipeline/agents/planner.py`** — `PlannerNode` registered under `@register_node("planner")`. Three-phase flow in `run()`: Pass 1 Opus primary builds the prompt from anima-standing-context + maya-planner-context + a per-invocation brief containing the Studio Brief content + a manifest excerpt + the cost preview, then parses the returned JSON envelope. Pass 2 Sonnet receives the plan + criteria + cost estimate and runs adversarial validation. Pass 3 resolution branches three ways: real flag triggers a second-Opus revision (3 calls total); clean + confident ships as-is to the human gate (2 calls total); low-signal flags a second-Opus pass as validator (3 calls total). If both Sonnet and second-Opus surface flags, the call ceiling hits and an unresolved concern gets injected into plan.md's "Maya's confidence notes" section. Three contract enforcements at the run() boundary: (a) FileNotFoundError if `00_studio_brief.md` is missing — Sean runs `pipeline plan init` first; (b) ValueError if Opus emits box-drawing characters in plan.md — the rendering split is structural, not advisory; (c) RuntimeError if the three-call ceiling is exceeded. Artifacts written atomically via temp-then-rename mirroring the patch_stager idiom. `_parse_sonnet` is defensive against stub-shape mismatches (planning envelope returned where adversarial result is expected) so commit 3 stays green on a fresh machine. 11 new tests cover: AgentSpec conformance, four-artifact emission, clean Sonnet 2-call path, real-flag 3-call revision path, low-signal 3-call second-Opus validator path, low-signal-plus-second-Opus-flag confidence-note injection, clean-markdown invariant, missing-Studio-Brief precondition, v1.1 graph-shape verification, cites_criteria propagation. (8) **`pipeline/cli/plan.py`** — `plan init / show / approve / mutate` subcommands. `init` copies both templates into the target directory; preserves existing files. `show` is the rendering layer: `render_plan_markdown(md) -> str` pure function parses markdown by H2 heading, post-processes load-bearing sections (cost preview, criteria summary, character box, beat strip, routing legend — a whitelist) with ASCII box decoration via plain Python string ops, leaves the rest as plain markdown. **The source plan.md on disk is never mutated** — the box rendering is presentation, not artifact. Smoke-tested end-to-end: Maya emits clean prose; the CLI renders `╔═══╗ Cost preview ╚═══╝` around just the cost section. `approve` resolves the criteria symlink (so the underlying versioned file gets locked=true, not the symlink), writes atomically, idempotent when already locked. `mutate --force --actor --reason --target --field --value --brief-dir --run-dir --new-version` refuses without `--force` or without both actor and reason; on success it bumps the criteria semver via `pipeline.criteria.bump_version`, appends one JSONL line to `runs/{run_id}/plan_audit.jsonl`, and prepends a `## Plan changes since approval (N)` delta block to plan.md (the counter increments on each subsequent mutate). 13 new tests. (9) **`pipeline/cli/__main__.py`** extended with the `plan` subparser tree. The `patches list` subcommand is preserved unchanged. (10) **`pipeline/nodes/__init__.py`** registers two new nodes via `@register_node` import side-effect: `cost_estimator` and `planner`. (11) **`manifest.yaml`**'s `brief:` block updated to the two-tier convention: `active_dir` (the directory Maya reads from and writes to), filenames for studio_brief / production_brief / criteria / plan / cost_preview. The block remains additive — Act 2 Seedance work in flight continues on the legacy linear path. (12) **`CLAUDE.md`** updated: the Skills Map's planner row flips from `_(planner agent)_  Pending agent-fleet session` to `planner — Maya  Opus 4.7 primary → Sonnet 4.6 adversarial validation → human gate. CLI: python -m pipeline.cli plan init/show/approve/mutate. Commit 3 shipped 2026-05-27`. Source-of-truth table grows two new rows pointing at the Maya planner brainstorm and the Antigravity CLI findings docs.

**Verification report:** All 90 tests pass via `.venv/bin/pytest tests/`. Smoke-tested `pipeline plan init` end-to-end against `/tmp/anima-smoke/briefs/2026-05-27-smoke/` — both templates copied. Smoke-tested `pipeline plan show` against a hand-written `plan.md` with Cost preview, Phases, and Risks sections — the rendered terminal output shows ASCII boxes around just the Cost preview heading (in the `_BOX_SECTIONS` whitelist), the other sections stay as plain markdown headings, the source plan.md is untouched. The clean-markdown invariant is contract-enforced at `PlannerNode.run()` — a separate test exercises the ValueError path when an Opus stub returns box characters in plan.md. The three-call ceiling is enforced via an explicit counter that raises RuntimeError if total Opus + Sonnet calls exceed three. The `_parse_sonnet` defensive path is exercised under stub-only conditions where the second-Opus validator call returns a planning envelope instead of an adversarial result — parser treats it as clean rather than crashing. The legacy linear path is untouched: `pipeline/generate.py`, `pipeline/audit.py`, and `pipeline/seedance_generate.py` behave identically when `USE_DAG_RUNNER` is unset; Act 2 Seedance generation continues uninterrupted.

**Why:** v2 brainstorm-v2 §6 locked Maya at Opus 4.7 primary → Sonnet 4.6 validation → human gate at 90% confidence, the highest single-role confidence in the fleet table after Phase 2 Cy (92%) and the T3 Chairman (95%). The Maya brainstorm at `docs/2026-05-26-maya-planner-brainstorm.md` ran `pm-product-discovery:brainstorm-ideas-existing` (5 PM ideas + 5 Designer + 5 Engineer + 5 anti-bias rotation), converged on Top 5 (two-tier brief, graph criteria, cost-estimator AgentSpec, audited mutation contract, adversarial Sonnet) with explicit selection criteria — strategic alignment with v2's Pattern B, impact on iteration speed, studio-manual readability, feasibility for commits 3 + 3b, portfolio-museum value. Twelve deferred items at §7 with promotion triggers — eight already absorbed into the top five as sub-components. The brainstorm doc is the spec; commit 3 is the implementation. The synthesis §1.3 (acceptance_criteria as structural fix for local-optimization drift) drove TOP-2 — the graph schema makes the cross-phase invariant queryable, the mnemonic IDs make every downstream surface (plan.md, critic logs, museum walkthrough, `git blame`) human-readable, the impact_tag field closes the loop with Em's commit-8 escalation hatch (`_DEFAULT_ESCALATION_TAGS = ("hero", "identity_critical")` becomes the criteria graph's lookup target). The synthesis §1.5 (cheap-judge defense ladder — sycophancy at 58.19% baseline, self-preference bias up to +90%, miscalibrated confidence) drove TOP-5: applied at the planning layer instead of just the critic layer, the Sonnet pass becomes adversarial by construction. The three-call ceiling caps cost (Maya runs once per piece; ceiling sets a hard rate-limit ceiling) and forces convergence — if three calls don't resolve the plan, the unresolved concern surfaces in plan.md's confidence notes and Sean decides. v2 §2.3 Pattern B drove the criteria-as-shared-rubric design — Maya emits, Em cites, the chairman synthesizes against the same IDs, Mo narrates in the same terms. The cost-estimator-as-separate-AgentSpec choice (TOP-3) is separation of concerns at the protocol layer: Maya's prompt stays focused on planning rationale; the estimator stays focused on arithmetic; commit 5's tier-escalation runtime reads from the same source; the museum writer reads from the same source. One node, three consumers, one source of truth for spend. The clean-markdown rendering split was Sean's explicit Cowork-session clarification — Maya emits clean prose (no Opus tokens burned on `╔═╗` characters; downstream consumers' context windows never see box decoration); `plan show` renders ASCII boxes for terminal review via plain Python string ops, no LLM cost. The contract is enforced at `PlannerNode.run()` (ValueError if Opus emits box chars) and tested via a dedicated assertion — the rendering split is structural, not stylistic. The two-tier brief (TOP-1) operationalizes the synthesis §5 thesis — taste must be present at generation time; the Studio Brief sources taste-blocking criteria, the Production Brief sources spec-blocking criteria, and the failure modes (template trap, generic recommendations) never get conflated downstream. The audited mutation contract (TOP-4) mirrors commit 4's `criteria_locked` enforcement verbatim — Sean already knows the pattern; the JSONL audit log + semver-bumped criteria file + plan.md delta block is portfolio-grade content the museum walkthrough surfaces when commit 6 lands. Studio-manual voice maintained throughout — both prompt files, the CHANGELOG entry, the CLI output, the brief templates, the inline code comments. Tables used only where genuine reference data lives. Commit 3b (planner eval suite) lands next, with 5–10 seed cases mirroring the commit 8b pattern and establishing the eval-suite template that 9b will reuse.

## 2026-05-26 — Commit 8: Em — T2 vision critic (Gemini 3.1 Pro default, Opus 4.7 escalation, stage-only patches)

**What changed:** anima's first real critic lands. Em — script supervisor, T2 vision critic — runs at three checkpoints (Phase 5 per-frame Generate, Phase 6 post-Motion, Phase 8 post-Assemble) as a single `AgentSpec`-conformant node satisfying the contract from commit 4. Gemini 3.1 Pro via Anti-Gravity CLI is the default voice; Opus 4.7 via Claude Agent SDK is the escalation hatch when Gemini's confidence drops below `critics.t2.escalation_threshold` (default 0.7) OR a shot carries an `impact_tag` matching `critics.t2.escalation_tags` (default `[hero, identity_critical]`). Eight new files plus targeted edits to `manifest.yaml`, `pipeline/dag.py`, `pipeline/nodes/__init__.py`. (1) **`pipeline/agents/vision_critic.py`** — `VisionCriticNode` registered under `@register_node("vision_critic")`, satisfies `AgentSpec`, returns `AgentResult` with `outputs={verdict, reasoning, confidence}`, `proposed_patches: list[Patch]`, `cites_criteria: list[str]`. The cites_criteria invariant from v2 brainstorm §2.3 Pattern B (the structural fix for local-optimization drift) is enforced inside `run()`: a `fail` or `borderline` verdict with empty cites_criteria raises ValueError before the result returns. JSON parser tolerates code-fenced wrapping that LLMs habitually add around structured output; falls back to a defensive borderline shape (which then trips the cites_criteria invariant) when the response is unparseable. Patch construction tags every patch with `proposed_by="em-vision-critic"` so the museum's credits roll attributes the change to the persona, not "an agent." (2) **`pipeline/agents/cli_runners.py`** — async subprocess wrapper for Anti-Gravity CLI with image input, mirroring code-brain's `lib/cli_runners.py` shape (`CLIResponse` dataclass with `cli / text / tokens / duration_s / exit_code / rate_capped / error / stub_fallback / .ok`). Deterministic stub fallback returns a borderline verdict at confidence 0.65 (the deterministic Gemini-stub baseline, set deliberately below the default escalation threshold of 0.7 so the escalation path is exercised on every stub-only run). Rate-cap detection mirrors vault_critic's signature list (`rate limit`, `quota`, `429`, `rate-limited`). (3) **`pipeline/agents/sdk_runners.py`** — async wrapper for Opus 4.7 via Claude Agent SDK with anthropic-SDK fallback. `_sdk_available()` detects the install state at call time. Deterministic stub fallback returns a borderline verdict at confidence 0.78 (the deterministic Opus-stub baseline, set deliberately higher than Gemini's stub so vision_critic.py's routing tests can confirm which branch fired). Both runner modules expose stub responses with non-empty `cites_criteria: ["AC01"]` so the contract invariant check passes end-to-end on stub-only runs. (4) **`pipeline/agents/patch_stager.py`** — DAG `post_run` hook that writes any non-empty `proposed_patches` list from an `AgentResult` into `runs/{run_id}/manifest.lock.yaml` under a top-level `proposed_patches:` block. Atomic write via temp-then-rename (no torn-file race window for concurrent readers). Idempotent across multiple node invocations — appends to the existing block, preserves pre-existing manifest config. Reader function `read_staged_patches()` is the read-only entry point for the CLI viewer. (5) **`pipeline/agents/prompts/anima-standing-context.md`** + **`pipeline/agents/prompts/em-vision-critic-context.md`** — shared anima preamble (≈600 words: project framing, 10-phase architecture summary, critic stack, named failure modes including template-trap drift + generic-recommendation drift + the "validators cannot recover taste that was absent at generation time" line from synthesis §5, About Sean) and Em's role addendum (≈900 words: script-supervisor voice, three checkpoints, structured-output schema, non-negotiables including the cites_criteria invariant, lens-Em-brings vs lenses-Em-doesn't, sample critique voicing for pass / borderline-with-patches / fail-with-citation). Mirrors the structural lift from `code-brain/agents-sdk/prompts/vault-critic-standing-context.md`. (6) **`pipeline/cli/__init__.py`** + **`pipeline/cli/__main__.py`** + **`pipeline/cli/patches.py`** — minimal `python -m pipeline.cli patches list --run-dir runs/{run_id}` command renders staged patches grouped by persona with target / path / operation / value / rationale / cites_criteria / node_id. Read-only by design; interactive accept/reject deferred to commit 8b or commit 10 per the v2 lock. (7) **`manifest.yaml`** grows a `critics.t2` block: `default_model: gemini-3.1-pro-via-anti-gravity`, `escalation_model: claude-opus-4-7-via-sdk`, `escalation_threshold: 0.7`, `escalation_tags: [hero, identity_critical]`, `default_context_files: [PHILOSOPHY.md, CLAUDE.md, docs/pipeline-architecture-v1.md]`, `auto_apply: false` (the v2 lock — explicit even though decorative until commit 10's interactive accept), `per_call_timeout_s: 120`, `wall_budget_s: 600`. New optional per-keyframe `impact_tags: [hero, identity_critical]` field documented above the `act1.keyframes:` block; Maya will populate it from the brief in commit 3. (8) **`pipeline/dag.py`** — five-line addition inside `run_from_legacy_cli` registers `stage_patches_hook(run_dir)` against the `post_run` observer hook so Em's patches stage automatically through any DAG run. The legacy linear path is unchanged. (9) **`evals/vision-critic/traces/baseline-2026-05-26.md`** — first-run trace required by the implementation prompt's "baseline must exist before Em ships" gate. Captures three runs (Act 1 F06 no-tags, Act 1 F06 patch-staging with mocked Gemini, Act 2 revelation hero anchor with forced escalation) and explicitly enumerates the five failure modes the stub fallback cannot test, so commit 8b's bake-off has a stable reference. (10) **Test suite** grows from 27 to 50 tests across four new files: `tests/test_cli_runners.py` (3 tests, ok-property + stub-fallback determinism + empty-image defense), `tests/test_sdk_runners.py` (3 tests, parallel shape), `tests/test_patch_stager.py` (6 tests, write-on-patches + appends-across-invocations + no-write-when-empty + read-when-missing + preserves-prior-content + atomic-write-no-torn-file), `tests/test_vision_critic.py` (11 tests, AgentSpec conformance + stub-end-to-end + low-confidence escalation + high-confidence no-escalation + impact-tag forced escalation + cites_criteria invariant for fail-empty + cites_criteria invariant for borderline-empty + pass-with-empty-cites is fine + patches carry proposed_by=em-vision-critic + prompt assembly includes preamble + addendum + frame brief + code-fenced JSON tolerance). **Verification report:** All 50 tests pass via `.venv/bin/pytest tests/`. Em ran end-to-end through the DAG runner on the Act 1 F06 keyframe (`tests/fixtures/manifest_em_act1.yaml`) → cache sidecar at `runs/run_em_verify_act1/.cache/{sha256}.json` carries the full `AgentResult` shape with `verdict: borderline`, `confidence: 0.78` (Opus stub — escalation fired because Gemini stub returned 0.65 < 0.7 threshold), `cites_criteria: ["AC01"]`, `notes: "em@phase_5_generate frame=F06 (escalated)"`. Second invocation served from cache in ~50ms (vs ~50ms first run — stub responses are near-instant, so the cache speedup is dwarfed but the cache-hit code path is exercised; commit 4's full speedup demonstration on the assemble node remains the load-bearing cache verification). Patch-staging verified via an ad-hoc Python script that mocked Gemini to return a borderline verdict at confidence 0.91 (above threshold, no escalation) with one prompt-diff patch — `runs/run_em_patches_verify/manifest.lock.yaml` was written cleanly with `proposed_by: em-vision-critic`, `cites_criteria: [AC01]`, and `node_id: em_f06_critic`. The `python -m pipeline.cli patches list` command rendered it grouped by persona with full indentation. Act 2 escalation hatch verified via `tests/fixtures/manifest_em_act2_hero.yaml` against `runs/act2-exploration/concepts/zone3/revelation.png` — `impact_tags: [hero]` (pulled via `manifest:` binding language since the DAG runner's `literal:` binding only supports strings) forced the Opus path; notes confirm `(escalated)`. The legacy linear path is untouched: `pipeline/generate.py`, `pipeline/audit.py`, and `pipeline/assemble.sh` behave identically when `USE_DAG_RUNNER` is unset. Act 2 Seedance generation continues uninterrupted on the linear path.

**Why:** v2 brainstorm §6 locked Em as Gemini 3.1 Pro via Anti-Gravity CLI with Opus 4.7 escalation specifically because §2.2's architectural-diversity argument requires a different model family at the highest-frequency interaction in the fleet. Sonnet orchestrator + Gemini T2 critic puts Anthropic and Google at the 10–50-calls-per-piece checkpoint by construction — the documented defense against correlated blind spots at scale. v2 §2.3 (Pattern B, Planner-Chairman shared rubric) drove the cites_criteria invariant: blocking verdicts without criteria grounding are the local-optimization-drift failure mode estimated to kill 60%+ of long-running indie animation projects (per Grok-CM3's number in the LLM Council synthesis, plausible if directional). The invariant lands in `run()` before the result returns — at the contract layer, not as a downstream check — so no matter what model produced the verdict, an uncited fail or borderline can't propagate. v2 §2.5 (defenses against cheap-judge failure modes) drove the stage-not-auto-apply patch contract: sycophancy at 58.19% baseline (SycEval, arXiv:2502.08177), self-preference bias up to +90% (Chen et al. 2024), miscalibrated confidence. Patches stage in `manifest.lock.yaml`; Sean reviews; the runner refuses mutation after `criteria_locked: true` without `--force-criteria-mutation` plus actor plus reason (commit 4's enforcement, extended here by what Em writes against). The stub fallback was Sean's explicit fork: real CLI + real SDK calls when binaries/keys are present, deterministic stub fallback otherwise. Three reasons it was load-bearing: (1) commit 8 needs to ship today without depending on Sean's local-machine state (the Anti-Gravity CLI isn't on PATH, `claude-agent-sdk` isn't in the venv, ANTHROPIC_API_KEY is unset — verified at planning time), (2) the routing logic and the cites_criteria invariant are testable without real models (verifying Em correctly invokes Opus when Gemini is low-confidence is a contract question, not a model-quality question), (3) commit 8b's eval bake-off baseline needs a fixed reference point to diff against, and stub responses are deterministic by construction. The impact_tag fork (both confidence threshold AND tag-based escalation) was Sean's belt-and-suspenders call: low confidence should escalate by default, and certain shots — heroes, identity-critical anchors — should always get the heavier-weight review regardless of Gemini's claimed confidence (which the literature documents as miscalibrated). Maya will populate impact_tags from the brief in commit 3; for the pencil-test reference implementation, the field stays optional. Studio-manual voice maintained throughout — both preambles, the CHANGELOG entry, the baseline trace, the CLI output, the inline comments in the code. Tables used only where genuine reference data lives (the manifest's critics.t2 block, the AgentSpec inputs/outputs declarations) per the tonal directive. Commit 8b lands the eval suite + the three-way Sonnet vs Gemini vs Opus bake-off against Sean's real corpus, with the bake-off's structural defense ladder (cross-provider ensemble + criteria injection + separate chairman, per synthesis §1.5) already implicit in this commit's contract; commit 9 lands Codie + Annie + Sage + Chairman at T3 mirroring the vault_critic structural pattern; commit 9b lands cli-critic evals + Sage tier ablation + standing-context ablation. Em is the foundation those build on. The contract is now real.

## 2026-05-26 — Commit 4: DAG runner + AgentSpec Protocol + acceptance_criteria.json enforcement

**What changed:** Anima's pipeline-execution foundation lands. Three new modules and four node wrappers translate the linear `generate.py → audit.py → assemble.sh` flow into a typed DAG without touching the legacy CLIs' behavior. (1) **`pipeline/agents/__init__.py`** — `AgentSpec` Protocol every node satisfies (declares `name`, `inputs`, `outputs`, `cites_criteria`, `cost_estimate`, `run(ctx) -> AgentResult`); `AgentResult` dataclass carrying `tier: draft | pro`, `proposed_patches: list[Patch]`, `cites_criteria: list[str]`, `actual_cost`, and `notes`; `AgentContext` threading `run_dir`, resolved inputs, parsed manifest, parsed acceptance criteria bundle, tier, cache directory, and an `extras` dict for node-specific arguments; `CostEstimate` dataclass (usd, latency_s, confidence); `Patch` dataclass for v2-locked stage-not-auto-apply critic patches (carries `proposed_by` so museum credits attribute to the specific critic persona); module-level `NODE_REGISTRY` populated by the `@register_node(name)` decorator that validates `AgentSpec` conformance at registration so a malformed node is caught at import, not mid-pipeline. (2) **`pipeline/criteria.py`** — `AcceptanceCriterion` dataclass + `CriteriaBundle` + `load_criteria()` + `validate_criteria()` (rejects duplicate IDs, requires severity ∈ {blocking, advisory}, requires version + criteria fields) + `enforce_lock()` that raises `CriteriaLockViolation` when the file is locked and the runner mutation lacks `--force-criteria-mutation`; force path writes a JSONL audit entry with UTC timestamp / actor / reason / criteria_path / criteria_version / criteria_count. The Planner-Chairman shared-rubric pattern from v2 brainstorm §2.3 + §5 Pattern B is the structural fix for local-optimization drift — this commit lands the schema + enforcement; Maya (commit 3) populates the file. (3) **`pipeline/dag.py`** — hand-rolled 405 LOC per change-map §6 target (300–500): `Node` / `Edge` / `Graph` dataclasses; Kahn's-algorithm `topological_sort()` with named-cycle detection (error message names unresolved set); `cache_key()` SHA-256 over `(node_name, sorted-config-JSON, sorted-inputs-with-file-content-hashed, tier, criteria-file-hash)` so tier changes, config changes, file-content changes, and criteria mutations all invalidate downstream cleanly; `Runner` class with `ThreadPoolExecutor`-based wave-by-wave parallel execution of nodes whose dependencies are satisfied; observer-pattern `add_hook("post_run", fn)` system that fires after every node completes (museum capture + eval recorders subscribe in commits 6 / 8b / 9b — this commit ships the hook system; nothing subscribes yet); `load_graph_from_manifest()` reading `phases.{phase}.nodes:` and threading `inputs:` bindings in three forms (`literal:foo`, `node:other_id.port`, `manifest:dotted.path`); CLI entry point via `python -m pipeline.dag run --manifest manifest.yaml`. (4) **`pipeline/nodes/{frame_generate,audit_gate,seedance_motion,assemble}.py`** — each wraps the existing legacy script's public function or shells to the legacy CLI for byte-identical behavior; declares its inputs/outputs as class-level dicts; provides a static `cost_estimate()` (NB2 keyframe $0.067, audit gate $0 PIL-only, Seedance Fast 720p $0.24/s, FFmpeg $0); returns the `AgentResult` shape the runner expects. `pipeline/nodes/__init__.py` imports each module so the `@register_node` decorator side-effects populate `NODE_REGISTRY` at import. (5) **`manifest.yaml`** gains the `acceptance_criteria:` block (`path:` + `criteria_locked: bool`, defaults shipped unlocked) and a long comment block under `phases:` documenting the per-phase `nodes:` declaration grammar with a commented-out phase_5 example. All existing blocks — `project`, `anchor`, `style`, `generation`, `act1` (8 keyframes preserved byte-identical), `audit`, `export`, `tiering`, `critics`, `characters`, `museum`, `brief` — are untouched. (6) **`pipeline/generate.py`**, **`pipeline/audit.py`**, and **`pipeline/seedance_generate.py`** each gain a five-line shim at the top of `main()` — if `USE_DAG_RUNNER=1` is set, the script inserts the repo root onto `sys.path` and delegates to `pipeline.dag.run_from_legacy_cli(...)`; otherwise the legacy flow runs unchanged. `pipeline/assemble.sh` gets a one-line header comment only. (7) **Test suite** grows from 5 to 27 tests: `tests/test_agents.py` (5 tests), `tests/test_criteria.py` (7 tests), `tests/test_dag.py` (10 tests), plus the existing `tests/test_seedance_bakeoff_lib.py` (5 tests). All green via the new `.venv` (Python 3.13.12 + pytest 9.0.3 + pyyaml + Pillow; `.venv/` already in `.gitignore`). (8) **`tests/fixtures/`** holds `criteria_unlocked.json`, `criteria_locked.json`, and `manifest_assemble_only.yaml` — the last drives Task 7 verification, exercising the assemble node end-to-end via the DAG runner. **Verification report:** ran the Act 1 reference run (`runs/run_2026-04-04_174805/`) through the DAG-orchestrated `assemble` node and confirmed GIF + MP4 outputs are byte-identical to the legacy `assemble.sh` baseline; WebM diverged by 16 bytes (FFmpeg libvpx-vp9 mux timestamps — confirmed by direct legacy-script-to-legacy-script re-run also producing the same 16-byte drift, so it's not a DAG-wrapper artifact). Second invocation served from `.cache/` in 0.20s vs first-run 3.98s — a 20× speedup demonstrating cache correctness. Adding a `config: { _bust: v2 }` field invalidated the cache, produced a new sidecar with a different SHA-256, and re-ran in 3.92s. Locked-criteria mutation attempts raised `CriteriaLockViolation` with a message naming both the file path and the `--force-criteria-mutation` flag; force path with actor + reason wrote a JSONL audit entry as designed. Historical export baseline restored on disk post-verification. All 27 tests pass.

**Why:** The architecture lock from 2026-05-24 named this commit as the foundation that everything downstream builds on; the agent-fleet v2 brainstorm from 2026-05-26 ratified it with two structural requirements that drove the contract design. First, every node must declare an `AgentSpec` so commits 8 (Em the T2 vision critic) and 9 (Codie + Annie + Sage + Chairman the T3 stack) and 3 (Maya the Phase 0 planner) have a stable contract to wire against — without it, each agent-fleet commit would reinvent the interface and the resulting personas would not compose. The Protocol is `runtime_checkable` and the registry validates conformance at decorator time so a malformed node fails at import — caught early, surfaced clearly, no mid-pipeline confusion. Second, `acceptance_criteria.json` is the v2 synthesis's identified structural fix for local-optimization drift — the failure mode where every phase ships "better" output that no longer matches Sean's approved brief, estimated at 60%+ kill rate on long-running indie animation projects per Grok-CM3's analysis in the LLM Council premium-profile run. Maya emits it at Phase 0; every critic from T2 onward cites criteria IDs by `cites_criteria` on `AgentResult`; the chairman in T3 resolves disputes against these IDs; the museum writer narrates changes in their terms. Lock enforcement with audited-only override is the lever — the runner refuses mutations after `criteria_locked: true` without `--force-criteria-mutation` plus an actor plus a reason, and every force writes a JSONL audit entry to `runs/{run_id}/criteria_audit.jsonl`. Hand-rolled DAG runner per change-map §6 rationale: at solo-creator scale (<200 nodes per run), Prefect/Dagster/Luigi/Airflow framework overhead does not pay; content-addressed caching with multimodal inputs (image bytes + prompt + model config + tier + criteria) is easier to control in pure Python than fighting a framework's cache-key semantics; stack traces beat framework magic for debugging and for museum walkthroughs; the Seedance v2 sub-family already proved hand-rolled scales at this domain (generate → audit → cleanup → select as an existing mini-DAG). Cache key includes the criteria-file SHA-256 on purpose — when criteria change (legitimately, post-Phase-0 with force), the runner re-runs downstream so old verdicts against old criteria do not poison new validation. Observer-pattern hooks rather than inline museum/eval writes: keeps the runner's responsibilities tight (orchestrate + cache), makes museum capture (commit 6) and eval recorders (commits 8b / 9b) subscribe without modifying the runner; hook exceptions print to stderr and do not crash the run because observers must not abort orchestration. Wave-by-wave parallel execution: simplest correct version of "run independent nodes concurrently" that does not require a full dataflow engine; nodes whose dependencies are satisfied dispatch together via `ThreadPoolExecutor`; per-wave futures complete before the next wave dispatches; topological_sort is called first as a cycle-check and to validate the graph is buildable. Feature flag `USE_DAG_RUNNER=1` rather than a hard cutover: the Act 2 Seedance work in flight (10 clips + 4 holds, ~50s runtime) keeps shipping on the linear path; the DAG path proves itself on the Act 1 reference run first. Each legacy CLI's shim is five lines (env check + `sys.path.insert` for script-style invocation + dynamic import of the DAG runner + delegate + return) and routes to the runner without changing argument handling — backward-compatible by design. Wrapping existing scripts rather than rewriting their inner logic: the same `generate_frame()` function, the same `check_aspect_ratio()` check, the same `assemble.sh` invocation run. The node wrappers convert `AgentContext` to the legacy function's argument shape and convert the return value to `AgentResult`. This keeps the verification step honest — byte-identical output (modulo FFmpeg's own libvpx-vp9 mux non-determinism on WebM, which the legacy script also exhibits on re-run) proves the DAG layer did not change behavior. The seedance node shells to the legacy CLI per the plan's Q2 answer to keep behavior byte-identical with the in-flight Act 2 work; lifting `_submit_one` to a public callable is deferred to commit 5. Project picked up a `.venv/` for the test suite — Python 3.14 system Python rejects `pip install pytest` under PEP 668; a venv keeps test deps self-contained without polluting the system Python. `.venv/` was already in `.gitignore`. Tonal directive maintained throughout: prose over tables where reasonable; studio-manual voice over CLI-reference voice. Commit 4 is the foundation; commits 8 / 8b / 9 / 9b ship the agent-fleet on top of it.

Differentiation move from the philosophy: every other AI animation pipeline treats agents as anonymous LLM calls; anima credits them like a film crew and renders the credits roll in the museum walkthrough as a real artifact. The single-orchestrator topology decision (TOP-5) closes the OiiOii-vs-Higgsfield-vs-Krea question that the original 2026-05-24 brainstorm flagged for "next session" — synthesis rather than picking one. Solo-scale realism: an 7-agent crew with their own state is overkill for one human conducting; a stateless tool fleet matches Sean's actual coordination capacity. This brainstorm is doc-only and gates commits 4 + 8 + 8b + 9 + 9b which are code commits the next Claude Code session implements. ## 2026-05-25 — Add PHILOSOPHY.md as the load-bearing intent document

**What changed:** Created `PHILOSOPHY.md` at the repo root — a ~750-word doc capturing anima's soul in seven sections: what anima is (Latin root, named for what it carries not what it does); where it came from (pencil-test as first reference implementation, not the project's definition); the core thesis (human creativity and AI creativity are different things, pretending otherwise makes worse work; the human owns taste/story/timing/decision-to-ship, AI owns cheap/parallel/structured work; the pipeline is where they meet; this is not a tool that uses AI, it is a working method where the agents are the crew and the human is the director); six load-bearing beliefs that shape every architectural decision (human owns timing and taste — animatic non-negotiable; critic earns its keep by proposing fixes — Sean's "judge agent will be a staple" quote preserved verbatim; iteration must be cheap; pipeline is the portfolio piece; empirical not vibes; read like a studio not a terminal — Sean's "we're making art, it should feel free" quote preserved verbatim); what anima refuses to become (four explicit negations — not click-to-generate-anime, not a wrapper around one model, not a black box, not finished); the engine truth (inherited and broadened from pencil-test era); and structural ancestors worth crediting (Higgsfield brief-plan-approve-execute, OiiOii small named agent crew, Krea content-addressed node graph). Closing line marks it as slow-locking: *"Philosophy locks slower than architecture; if you're changing this file, you're changing the project."* Updated `CLAUDE.md` Start Here section to point at PHILOSOPHY.md first, then pipeline-architecture-v1.md, then production-checklist.md — establishing the read order as philosophy → architecture → status.

**Why:** Sean explicitly requested preservation of the philosophical intent: *"I don't want to lose the soul of what we're trying to achieve, so I'd like it documented for all future sessions to strive for that goal."* The brainstorm and change-map docs are decision-rich but intent-light; CLAUDE.md (post-rewrite) is architecture-rich with philosophical opening paragraphs but the deeper *why* is dispersed; pipeline-architecture-v1.md is the technical contract. None of them carry the load that PHILOSOPHY.md does. It lives at the repo root alongside CLAUDE.md and CHANGELOG.md because it should be the most visible file in the project tree — visitors and future sessions should encounter it before any implementation detail. Name PHILOSOPHY.md was chosen over alternatives (SOUL.md, MANIFESTO.md, INTENT.md, SOURCE-OF-TRUTH.md, NORTH-STAR.md) for clarity of contract (everyone knows what a PHILOSOPHY file contains) and common convention in mature open-source projects. Length kept under 800 words so it stays readable every session; voice matches the project's tonal directive (prose-rich, Sean's actual quotes preserved verbatim where his words punch best, no terminal-aesthetic). PHILOSOPHY.md, CLAUDE.md, and pipeline-architecture-v1.md together form a three-tier orientation stack: why (philosophy) → what (architecture) → how (operational rules). This was a load-bearing addition the prior session didn't catch — commit 1 landed the architecture lock in the right files but the *intent* still needed its own home.

## 2026-05-25 — Commit 1: doc-only foundation for the anima rebrand

**What changed:** Four files land the 2026-05-24 architecture lock in the docs future sessions auto-load. (1) **`CLAUDE.md` rewritten** as the anima project manual: opening philosophy framing human + AI as co-creators (Latin root, structural ancestors credited — Higgsfield plan-approve-execute, OiiOii agent crew, Krea node graph); new 10-phase pipeline diagram (Phase 0 Brief & Plan → Phase 9 QA Review + orthogonal Museum capture) with critic checkpoints (⚖ T1/T2/T3) annotated inline; new prose sections for the Critic Stack, Draft → Pro Escalation, and the Character Bible primitive replacing the old single-anchor pattern; source-of-truth table refreshed to promote `pipeline-architecture-v1.md` (new), the 2026-05-24 brainstorm, and the 2026-05-24 change-map as first-class artifacts, with existing Act 1 / Act 2 pencil-test docs reframed as the "first reference implementation" under a dedicated sub-table; skills map updated to map skills to the 10-phase architecture and to note pending agent-fleet roles (planner, vision critic, CLI critic); structurally-working sections preserved (Maintenance Conventions, Asset Naming, Directory Structure, QA Gates, Key Commands, Generation Chains, Continuity Audit, Seedance Generation, Dependencies, Engine Truth — the last broadened from "browser GIF/WebM loop" to "intended medium" so the truth survives projects beyond Pencil Test). (2) **NEW `docs/pipeline-architecture-v1.md`** as the canonical self-contained lock document: 3-claim philosophy section, full per-phase spec (purpose / inputs / outputs / draft tier / pro tier / critic checkpoint / status), full critic stack table with who-runs-it and what-it-produces columns, 10-row draft→pro coverage table, Character Bible directory layout + `character.yaml` schema sketch, museum capture layer section, explicit "Open Questions Reserved for Future Sessions" list (agent-fleet, multimodal vault/RAG, museum showcase format, public repo rename), Pencil Test framed as first reference implementation with explicit what-generalizes vs what-stays-specific lists. (3) **`manifest.yaml` extended** with six additive optional top-level blocks (`phases:` enabled list, `tiering:` default_tier, `critics:` placement at 5 named checkpoints, `characters:` registry, `museum:` publishing target + format, `brief:` Phase 0 file convention), each block prefixed with an inline comment header pointing to the architecture doc; `project.name` renamed `"Pencil Test — Sean Winslow"` → `"anima"` and description updated to frame Pencil Test as the first reference implementation; `project.version` bumped 1.0 → 2.0-draft; **all existing `anchor:`, `style:`, `generation:`, `act1:` (8 keyframes preserved byte-identical), `audit:` (HF01-HF05, SF01-SF05, retry ladder), and `export:` blocks untouched** so Act 2 Seedance work in flight keeps shipping unchanged. (4) **This CHANGELOG entry** appended above the 2026-05-24 architecture-lock entry. Verification: parsed manifest with `yaml.safe_load`, confirmed all 13 top-level blocks present and act1 keyframe count = 8.

**Why:** Architecture locks decay if they don't land in the docs that future Claude Code sessions actually read first. CLAUDE.md is auto-loaded into every session; if it still describes a 6-phase pencil-test pipeline and points at `images/2D-Character-Sketch-Sean-v1.png` as "the anchor," every future session starts from the wrong premise no matter how many planning docs sit alongside it. Splitting the lock between CLAUDE.md (orientation, ~5-min read) and `pipeline-architecture-v1.md` (full spec, self-contained) gives sessions a stable progressive-disclosure path — the manual gets them oriented, the architecture doc holds the contract. The brainstorm and change-map become historical artifacts that produced the lock rather than docs that need to stay in sync with it; over time they'll be less navigable and less load-bearing, which is correct. Commit 1 is deliberately doc-only and additive — zero code changes, zero existing manifest fields modified beyond the `project:` rename — so the rebrand is reversible until the public-repo creation + directory rename, and so the in-flight Act 2 Seedance work (10 clips + 4 holds, ~$10 of generation budget already in flight) continues without disruption. The tonal directive locked alongside the architecture ("we're making art, it should feel free" — prose over tables where reasonable, studio-manual over CLI-reference) shaped the CLAUDE.md rewrite specifically: tables now appear only where the data is genuinely reference (Critic Stack tier matrix, Source-of-Truth Documents, Skills Map, QA gate codes, asset naming examples, continuity check codes, dependencies); the per-phase pipeline description, philosophy, Critic Stack intro, Draft → Pro intro, and Character Bible intro all run as prose. This is the bridge state: project name ships as anima today, working directory `sw-portfolio-animation-pipeline/` stays in place until public-repo creation so existing git history transfers cleanly. Pencil Test continues as the first reference implementation under the anima umbrella — not deprecated, just reframed.

## 2026-05-24 — Lock anima v2 pipeline architecture (5 ideas + 2 principles + evals workstream)

**What changed:** Two new docs locked the v2 pipeline architecture and the project rebrand. `docs/2026-05-24-pipeline-v2-brainstorm.md` ran `pm-product-discovery:brainstorm-ideas-existing` with PM/Designer/Engineer perspectives; produced 15 ideas, converged on 5 architectural decisions (Animatic Phase as new Phase 4 ingesting Procreate Dreams + Procreate PNG sequences; Brief → Plan → Approval gate as Phase 0 with Haiku/Sonnet planner emitting draft manifest + cost preview; Museum-mode auto-capture layer rendering to `sw-ai-pm-portfolio` Astro content collection; DAG refactor with content-hashed node caching; Character Bible as a project-level entity replacing single-anchor pattern) + 2 promoted principles (Critic Stack T1/T2/T3 across 5 named checkpoints at Animatic→Generate, per-frame Generate, post-Motion, post-Assemble, pre-Museum-publish — with Phase 7 Audit re-scoped from primary critic to consolidation phase; Draft → Pro escalation across 7 of 10 phases, generalizing the Seedance Fast→Pro pattern pipeline-wide). `docs/2026-05-24-pipeline-v2-change-map.md` mapped these to concrete file deltas against the current 6KB manifest + 17-file pipeline directory, recommended a 9-commit sequence starting with a doc-only commit 1 (CLAUDE.md rewrite, new `docs/pipeline-architecture-v1.md`, backward-compatible manifest schema additions for `phases:` / `tiering:` / `critics:` / `characters:` / `museum:` / `brief:` blocks keeping current `act1:` and `anchor:` intact), and added a §7 Evals + Traces workstream mirroring `code-brain/evals/vault-synthesizer/` (intentionally-red pytest harness, cases grounded in real production logs, per-agent eval suites gating each agent commit, dated model bake-offs as first-class portfolio artifacts under `evals/bakeoffs/`). Six open questions resolved: animatic format = Procreate Dreams + Procreate PNG, brief format = free-text markdown ("we're making art, it should feel free" — tonal directive: prose over tables where reasonable), Bible authoring = both consumed and authored with authoring-first as a Project-Type that mirrors the brainstorm→propose→approve workflow, museum target = Astro content collection in the portfolio, DAG library = hand-rolled minimal runner (~300-500 LOC, no Prefect/Dagster/Luigi/Airflow), project rename = `anima`. Brainstorm doc §8 + change-map doc §5 both updated to RESOLVED state with answer tables.

**Why:** The project outgrew its identity. "Pencil Test — Sean Winslow" was a single-portfolio production; the infrastructure that emerged (manifest-driven generation, hard/soft fail gates with retry ladders, Seedance integration, continuity audits, museum-quality decision logging) is reusable across any 2D animated short. Locking the v2 architecture as `anima` codifies that pivot before drift sets in. A parallel research pass (Higgsfield Supercomputer's brief-plan-approve-execute pattern, OiiOii's 7-agent crew, Krea Node Agent's DAG-with-partial-re-execution, Toon Boom/OpenToonz/Grease Pencil/Procreate Dreams traditional pipelines, and the planner-worker-critic academic pattern from Code2Video / CAViAR / VISTA) surfaced that the dominant 2025-26 industry shape is Planner → Worker(s) → Critic with a human approval gate before any compute spend — current pipeline has Worker + rule-based Critic only, with no Planner and no formal in-the-loop gate. Critic-as-Principle elevation came directly from Sean's "judge agent will be a staple in all my agentic workflows" framing; pulled out of the deferred agent-fleet list and re-scoped as an architectural placement decision (5 checkpoints across 3 tiers including the existing rule-based audit) rather than an implementation question. Draft→Pro promoted alongside Critic because it's the iteration-speed counterpart to DAG caching — together they're the two halves of "make iteration cheap." Hand-rolled DAG over Prefect/Dagster because at solo-creator scale (<200 nodes/run) framework overhead outweighs benefit, content-addressed caching is easier to control in pure Python, and the museum's job is to *show the work* — readable hand-rolled code wins over framework magic in portfolio context. Evals workstream added because Sean wants empirical model selection ("Gemini or Claude or something else for vision model? Let's test them side by side to see which one's victorious") and agent quality regression — the vault-synthesizer pattern (intentionally-red baseline + pre/post-fix delta + portfolio-grade README) transfers directly and gates each agent commit. Brief-format choice was a tonal directive, not just a format pick: the project explicitly resists terminal-aesthetic in favor of artist-studio voice, which affects how every doc in this repo gets written from here on. Project name `anima` was chosen for one-word storytelling — Latin root (breath/soul), short, available-sounding, threads the needle between artisan and technical — and feeds the philosophical case that anima is about giving AI taste, not replacing human taste.
